مساقات میں امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر اور دلیل
وقال الشافعى المعاملة جائزة ولا يجوز المزارعة الا تبعا للمعاملة لان الاصل في هذا المضاربة والمعاملة اشبه بها لان فيه شركة فى الزيادة دون الاصل وفى المزارعة لو شرط الشركة في الربح دون البذر بان شرط رفعه من راس الخارج يفسد فجعلنا المعاملة أصلا و جوزنا المزارعة تبعا لها كالشرب في بيع الارض والمنقول فى وقف العقار
ترجمہ اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ مساقات جائز ہے اور مزارعت جائز نہیں ہے مگر مساقات کے تابع ہو کر اسلئے کہ اصل اس میں مضاربت ہے اور مساقات کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے اس لئے کہ مساقات میں زیادتی کے اندر شرکت ہے نہ کہ اصل میں اور مزارعت میں اگر نفع کے اندر شرکت کی شرط کی جائے نہ کہ پیج میں اس طریقہ پر کہ پیداوار کی اس سے بیج کو اٹھانے کی شرط کی جائے تو عقد مزارعت فاسد ہو جاتا ہے تو ہم نے مساقات کو اصل قرار دیا اور مزارعت کو مساقات کے تابع بنا کر جائز قرار دیا جیسے زمین کی بیع میں شرب اور زمین کے وقف میں منقول ۔ تشریح یہ پوری عبارت امام شافعی کا مسلک اور دلیل بیان کرنے کیلئے ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مزارعت تو جائز نہیں ہاں مساقات جائز ہے۔ البتہ اگر مزارعت مساقات کے تابع ہوتو بر بناء تبعیت مزارعت بھی جائز ہے۔
مثلاً ایک باغ ہے جس کے دو حصوں میں درخت ہیں اور ایک حصہ میں خالی زمین پڑی ہوئی ہے تو عامل کو باغ کے ساتھ وہ زمین بھی دے دی کہ اسمیں کھیتی کرے تو جائز ہے ورنہ استقلالاً مزارعت جائز نہیں ہے۔
اب امام شافعی دلیل بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ مضاربت بالا تفاق جائز ہے اب ان دونوں میں سے مضاربت کے ساتھ جس کی مشابہت زیادہ ہو وہ جائز ہوگا۔
اور جب ہم نے غور کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ مضاربت کے ساتھ مساقات کو زیادہ مشابہت ہے کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ مضاربت میں رأس المال میں مضارب کی کوئی شرکت نہیں ہوتی بلکہ نفع میں ہوتی ہے اور یہی حال مساقات میں ہے کہ عامل کی کوئی شرکت راس المال یعنی باغ میں نہیں ہوتی بلکہ پھلوں میں شرکت ہوتی ہے اور مزارعت اس کے برعکس ہے کہ وہاں بیج میں شرکت ہوتی ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر بیج والا یہ شرط لگائے کہ میں پہلے اپنے پیج کی مقدار پیداوار سے لوں گے تو مزارعت فاسد ہو جاتی ہے الہذا ثابت ہوا کہ مضاربت کے ساتھ مساقات کا زیادہ جوڑ ہے تو ہم نے مساقات کو جائز کہا اور مزارعت کو نا جائز۔
البتہ تبعیت کے طریقہ پر مزارعت جائز ہے اور استقلال و تبعیت کے اعتبار سے بسا اوقات احکام میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے شرب کی بیع مستقلاً جائز نہیں مگر زمین کے تابع کر کے جائز ہے جیسے حمام وقف کیا تو اس کے ساتھ اس کے لوٹے وغیرہ کا وقف بھی جائز ہے۔
تنبیہ منقول کا استقلالا و قیمت تعامل کی وجہ سے جائز ہے تفصیل کیلئے دیکھئے شامی ص ۳۷۴ ج ۳۔
(Heading) Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint and evidence in musaqah. And Shafi'i said: The mu'amalah (musaqah) is permissible, but muzara'ah is not permissible except as a subordinate to mu'amalah, because the basis in this is mudarabah, and mu'amalah is more similar to it because it involves partnership in the increase without the principal, while in muzara'ah, if partnership in profit is stipulated without the seed, such that the seed is taken from the produce, it becomes invalid. So we made mu'amalah the principal and allowed muzara'ah as its subordinate, like the right to drink in sale of land and movables in waqf of real estate. Translation: And Shafi'i said that musaqah is permissible and muzara'ah is not permissible except subordinate to musaqah... Explanation: This entire passage is to explain Imam Shafi'i's position and evidence... For example, a garden with trees in two parts and empty land in one part; if the worker is given that land to cultivate along with the garden, it is permissible, otherwise independent muzara'ah is not permissible... [continues] Note: Movables independently are permissible due to custom; for details see Shami 3:374.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Shafi'i's argument for why musaqah (sharecropping of trees) is intrinsically valid while muzara'ah (sharecropping of land) is not, unless it accompanies musaqah. Shafi'i begins by stating his ruling: mu'amalah (i.e., musaqah) is permissible, but muzara'ah is not permissible except as subordinate to it. His evidence is based on analogy (qiyas) with mudarabah (silent partnership). The key similarity is that in both mudarabah and musaqah, the worker (factor) does not share in the principal capital (the tree or the capital) but only in the profit (fruit or profit). In contrast, in muzara'ah, the worker often shares in the seed (principal), which makes it more akin to a lease. Shafi'i supports this by noting that if a contract for muzara'ah stipulates that the seed is taken from the produce first, the contract becomes invalid, indicating that mixing seed with profit is problematic. Therefore, musaqah is analogous to mudarabah and is valid as an independent contract, while muzara'ah is only valid when it is subordinate to musaqah, such as when a garden contains both trees and empty land, and the worker cultivates the land alongside tending the trees. The author then provides an Urdu commentary explaining Shafi'i's reasoning in detail, including examples from sale of water rights and waqf of movables. The passage concludes with a note that movable property can be transacted independently due to customary practice, referencing Shami for further details.

Key Terms
المعاملة (al-mu'amalah): In this context, it refers specifically to musaqah (sharecropping of trees), as distinct from muzara'ah.
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared as agreed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Shafi'i as presented in this passage, under what condition is muzara'ah permissible?
A) When it is an independent contract with clearly defined seed and profit shares.
B) When it is subordinate to musaqah (sharecropping of trees).
C) When the duration of the contract is specified.
D) When the worker provides both labor and seed.

Key Takeaway
In Shafi'i's view, musaqah inherits autonomy from mudarabah, while muzara'ah requires attachment to musaqah to be valid — a clear example of how qiyas and the concept of subordination shape contracts.

Musaqah: Qiyas Requires Duration, but Istihsan Overrides
Discusses whether specifying duration is necessary for musaqah, with istihsan allowing it without stated duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi fiqh applies istihsan to dispense with the condition of duration in musaqah, and identify the types of crops to which this ruling extends.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas in musaqah because fruit ripens at a known time, eliminating uncertainty.

This passage explores the tension between analogical reasoning (qiyas) and juristic preference (istihsan) in the context of musaqah contracts. While qiyas treats musaqah as a lease requiring a specified term, istihsan permits the contract without a fixed duration when the crop's harvest time is naturally known. The author extends this logic to crops like berseem, whose seed maturation has a definite endpoint.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling by qiyas
Qiyas analogizes musaqah to a lease (ijarah), requiring a specified duration to avoid uncertainty (gharar). The author states that stipulating duration is the qiyas ruling.
This is similar to the condition in muzara'ah (sharecropping of land).
2
State the istihsan ruling and its scope
Istihsan allows musaqah without a fixed duration. The contract then applies to the first fruit that appears, because fruit has a known ripening time with little variation.
The contract ends naturally when that fruit is harvested.
3
Understand the basis for istihsan
The key is that fruit's ripening time is a known, fixed endpoint, eliminating the uncertainty (jahalah) that would otherwise invalidate the lease-like contract.
This reasoning differs from annual crops, where start and end vary by season.
4
Apply the same reasoning to other crops
The text extends the istihsan ruling to berseem (ratbah) and garlic, where the seed's maturation has a known endpoint (the final seed harvest). Thus, no duration specification is needed.
This shows the rule is not limited to fruit trees but applies to any crop with a definite, observable end.
5
Contrast with regular cultivation (muzara'ah)
In regular cultivation, the start varies by season (autumn, summer, spring), and the end depends on the start, creating uncertainty. Therefore, duration must be specified in muzara'ah.
This contrast highlights why istihsan applies to musaqah but not to muzara'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مساقات کیلئے مدت شرط ہے یا نہیں
و شرط المدة قياس فيها لانها اجارة معنى كما فى المزارعة وفى الاستحسان اذا لم يبين المدة يجوز ويقع على اول ثمر يخرج لان الثمر لإدراكها وقت معلوم وقل ما يتفاوت ويدخل فيها ما هو المتيقى
ترجمہ اور مساقات میں مدت کی شرط قیاس ہے اسلئے کہ مسافات معنی اجارہ ہے جیسے مزارعت میں اور استحسان میں جبکہ مدت بیان نہ کی جائے تو مساقات جائز ہے اور یہ عقدان پہلے پھلوں پر واقع ہو گا جو پیدا ہوں اسلئے کہ پھل ان کے پکنے کا ایک معلوم وقت ہے اور تفاوت کم ہوتا ہے اور مساقات میں وہ پھل داخل ہوں گے جو متیقن ہیں ۔
تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ تھا کہ مساقات کے اندر بھی مدت بیان کی جاتی جیسے مزارعت کے اندر شرط ہے۔ کیونکہ جیسے مزارعت ابتد او اجارہ ہے ایسے ہی مساقات بھی ابتداء اجارہ ہے لیکن مساقات میں نہ بنا و استحسان قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا گیا اور مدت کو بیان کیئے بغیر مساقات کو جائز قرار دیا گیا۔ کیونکہ پھلوں کے پکنے کا وقت معلوم و معروف ہے بخلاف کھیتی کے اور جب مدت بیان نہ کی جائے تو عقد پہلے پھلوں پر واقع ہو گا کیونکہ پہلے پھل متیقن ہیں۔ (و بیتا القول المفتی بہ فی الزراعة ) برسیم یا لہسن کی جب آخری لورہ گئی تو زمین والے نے کسی عامل سے کہا تم اس بریم یا لہسن کی حفاظت کرو یہاں تک کہ پیج آجائے اور جو بیج ہو گا وہ ہمارے تمہارے درمیان مشترک ہو گا مدت ضروری ہے یا نہیں
وإدراك البذر في أصول الرطبة فى هذا بمنزلة ادراك الثمار لان له نهايه معلومة فلا يشترط بيان المدة بخلاف الزرع لان ابتداءه يختلف كثيرا خريفا وصيفاً وربيعا والانتهاء بناء عليه فتدخله الجهالة
ترجمہ اور گند نے کھجڑوں میں بیج کا پکنا میان مدت کے سلسلہ میں پھلوں کے پکنے کے درجہ میں ہے اسلئے کہ اس کیلئے نہایت معلومہ ہے تو مدت کا بیان شرط نہیں ہے بخلاف کھیتی کے اسلئے کہ اس کی ابتداء بہت مختلف ہو جاتی ہے خریف اور صیف اور بیج کے اعتبار سے اور انتہاء ابتداء پر مبنی ہے تو کھیتی میں جہالت داخل ہو جائے گی۔
تشریح رطبہ کا ترجمہ یہاں گندنا سے کیا گیا ہے جو ایک گھاس ہے مگر سکب الانہرص ۴۲۹ ج ۲ پر ہے وفى الرطبة وهي بلغة مصر البرسیم یعنی رطبہ وہ ہے جس کو ہم برسیم کہتے ہیں اور یہ وہ گھاس ہے جو سردیوں کے موسم میں ہوتا ہے اور بھوسہ یا گوے کی کئی کے ساتھ ملا کر اس کو کھلایا جاتا ہے۔ جو لہسن کے مشابہ ہے۔ ان دونوں کو کاٹتے رہتے ہیں اور اوائل صیف تک ان کی لو بار بار آتی ہے اور کاشتکار آخری لوکو پیج کیلئے روک لیتے ہیں جو ہمارے کھیتوں میں کثرت سے ہوتی ہے۔
خريف .. موسم خزاں، یعنی پت جھڑ جو گرمی اور جاڑے کے درمیان کا موسم ہوتا ہے۔
(Heading) Is duration a condition in musaqah or not? And stipulating duration is [required] by qiyas, because it is a lease in meaning, as in muzara'ah. But by istihsan, if the duration is not specified, it is permissible, and it applies to the first fruit that appears, because fruit has a known time for ripening and little variation, and what is certain enters into it. Translation: And in musaqah, stipulating duration is by qiyas, because musaqah is like a lease in meaning, similar to muzara'ah. But by istihsan, when duration is not specified, musaqah is valid, and the contract operates on the first fruit produced, because fruit has a known time of ripening and variation is minimal, and the certain fruit enters. Explanation: The author says that qiyas required that duration be specified in musaqah as it is required in muzara'ah, because both are essentially ijarah. However, in musaqah, due to istihsan, the qiyas is abandoned and musaqah is permitted without specifying duration, because the ripening time of fruit is known, unlike cultivation. When duration is not specified, the contract applies to the first fruit because it is certain. (And the relied-upon view in agriculture is this.) For berseem or garlic, when the last harvest is done, the landowner tells a worker: 'Take care of this berseem or garlic until the seed comes, and whatever seed is produced will be shared between us.' Is duration necessary or not? And the ripening of the seed in the roots of the ratbah plant is in this regard like the ripening of fruits, because it has a known limit, so specifying duration is not required. Unlike cultivation, because its beginning varies greatly: autumn, summer, and spring, and the end depends on the beginning, so ignorance enters. Translation: And the ripening of the seed in the roots of ratbah is in the same position as the ripening of fruits regarding duration, because it has a known end, so specifying duration is not required, unlike cultivation because its beginning varies greatly: autumn, summer, spring, and the end is based on that, so ignorance enters. Explanation: Ratbah is translated here as 'gandana' (a type of grass), but in Skab al-Anhur 2:429 it says ratbah in Egyptian dialect is berseem, which is the grass that grows in winter and is fed to animals mixed with straw. It resembles garlic. These are cut repeatedly, and their yield comes repeatedly until early summer, and farmers keep the last yield for seed, which is common in our fields. Khareef: autumn season, between summer and winter.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage addresses whether musaqah (sharecropping of trees) requires a specified duration to be valid. The author begins by stating the ruling according to qiyas: stipulation of duration is required because musaqah is a lease (ijarah) in meaning, just like muzara'ah (sharecropping of land). However, by istihsan (juristic preference), if the duration is not specified, the contract is valid, and it applies to the first fruit that appears. The reasoning is that fruit has a known time of ripening with little variation, so there is no uncertainty (jahalah) about when the contract ends. The author then provides an Urdu commentary explaining that qiyas would require duration, but istihsan overrides it because the ripening time of fruit is well-known, unlike the cultivation of crops which depends on seasons. The passage then introduces a practical example: In the case of berseem (a type of clover) or garlic, when the last harvest is taken, the landowner may ask a worker to care for the crop until the seed is produced, with a share in the seed. The question is whether a specific duration must be stipulated. The author explains that for such plants, the ripening of the seed is like the ripening of fruit because it has a known endpoint (when the seed is ready). Therefore, specifying duration is not required, unlike regular cultivation where the start varies greatly with seasons, leading to uncertainty. The Urdu commentary further clarifies the meaning of 'ratbah' as berseem, a winter grass, and explains that it is similar to garlic in that they are harvested multiple times until the final seed crop. The passage concludes with a definition of 'khareef' (autumn).

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that in musaqah, since it is like a lease, duration must be specified.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that leads to abandoning qiyas in favor of a more flexible ruling due to custom or necessity.
رطبہ (ratbah): A type of grass (berseem/clover) harvested multiple times, with a known harvesting season.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does istihsan allow musaqah without a specified duration?
A) Because the contract is a gift, not a lease.
B) Because fruit has a known ripening time with little variation, eliminating uncertainty.
C) Because the parties can cancel at any time.
D) Because the worker is considered a volunteer.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan overrides qiyas in musaqah, making duration unnecessary when the crop has a known harvest endpoint.

intermediate
6 min
Duration in Musaqah: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Explains duration condition in musaqah with istihsan exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school allows musaqah without specifying duration and apply the same principle to bersim and garlic.

Core Idea
Istihsan permits musaqah without a fixed duration because fruit ripening time is known and uniform.

In this passage, the commentator explains a key Hanafi exception: while analogical reasoning (qiyas) would require a fixed duration in musaqah (like in ijarah), juristic preference (istihsan) allows it to be omitted. The reason is that fruits have a predictable ripening period, eliminating significant uncertainty. The same reasoning extends to plants like bersim (alfalfa) and garlic, whose seed maturation times are also known. This lesson walks you through the legal reasoning and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the dispute is about whether specifying duration (mudda) is required for the validity of a musaqah contract.
2
State the qiyas ruling
By qiyas, musaqah is analogous to ijarah, which requires a fixed term to avoid gharar. Therefore, qiyas would mandate a stated duration.
3
State the istihsan ruling
By istihsan, the contract is valid without specifying duration because the ripening time of fruit is known and rarely varies, so no significant uncertainty exists.
Istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.
4
Apply to rutba (bersim) and garlic
Like fruit, bersim and garlic have a known seed maturation time, so the same istihsan applies: no fixed duration needed.
The contract falls on the first fruit or seed that emerges.
5
Contrast with cultivation (muzara'ah)
For regular crops, planting times vary greatly (autumn, spring, etc.), causing uncertainty. Therefore, duration must be specified in muzara'ah.
Exception: In regions where the agricultural cycle is uniform, fatwa may allow omission.

بر تیم یا لہسن کی جب آخری لورہ گئی تو زمین والے نے کسی عامل سے کہا کہ تم اس برسیم ولہسن کی حفاظت کرو یہاں تک بیج آ جائے اور جو بیچ ہو گا وہ ہمارے اور تمہارے درمیان مشترک ہو گا تو بیان مدت کے بغیر یہ عقد جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ جس طرح پھلوں کے پکنے کا معلوم وقت ہے ایسے ہی برسیم اور لہسن کے بیج کے وقت معلوم ہے اسلئے بیان مدت کی شرط نہ ہو گی۔ اور کھیتی کا مسئلہ اس کے خلاف ہے، کیونکہ کھیتی میں تو ابتداء میں اختلاف کثیر ہوتا ہے اور جب ابتداء میں اختلاف ہو اور انتہاء میں بھی اختلاف ضرور ہوگا۔ تو یہاں مدت مجبول ہوگی اسلئے زراعت میں بیان مدت شرط ہے۔

Book of Musaqah. Note: The transmitted position is that it is valid independently and due to customary value; see Shami vol. 3 p. 374 for detail. Is duration a condition for musaqah? And stipulation of duration is by qiyas because it is a lease in meaning, as in muzara'ah. And by istihsan, if he does not specify the duration, it is valid and applies to the first fruit that emerges because fruit has a known time for ripening and rarely varies, and what is certain enters into it. Translation: And in musaqah, stipulation of duration is by qiyas because musaqah is a lease in meaning like in muzara'ah. And by istihsan, when duration is not stated, musaqah is valid and the contract falls on the first fruit that emerges because fruit has a known time for ripening and variation is little, and what is certain enters into it. Commentary: The author says that qiyas required that duration be stated in musaqah as it is a condition in muzara'ah because just as muzara'ah is initially a lease, so is musaqah initially a lease. But in musaqah, istihsan abandoned qiyas and declared musaqah valid without stating duration because fruit ripening time is known and well-known, unlike cultivation. And when duration is not stated, the contract falls on the first fruit because the first fruit is certain. (And the relied-upon statement in agriculture) When the last cutting of bersim or garlic has been taken, the landowner said to a worker: take care of this bersim or garlic until the seed comes, and whatever seed there is will be shared between us. Is duration necessary or not? And ripening of seed in the roots of rutba is equivalent to ripening of fruits in this regard because it has a known end, so stating duration is not a condition, unlike cultivation because its beginning varies greatly in autumn, summer, and spring, and the end is based on the beginning, so ignorance enters it. Translation: And the ripening of seed in the roots of the rutba plant is in the rank of ripening of fruits regarding the duration because it has a known end, so stating duration is not a condition, unlike cultivation because its beginning varies greatly according to autumn, summer, and spring, and the end is based on the beginning, so ignorance enters into cultivation. Commentary: The translation of rutba here is 'gandana' which is a grass, but in Shir'at al-Islam vol. 2 p. 429 it is: 'and rutba in Egyptian language is bersim' meaning rutba is what we call bersim, and it is the grass that grows in winter and is fed mixed with straw or something. It resembles garlic. Both are cut repeatedly and their yield comes repeatedly until early summer, and farmers keep the last yield for seed, which is abundant in our fields. Autumn: the season of fall, i.e. autumn which is the season between summer and winter. Summer: the hot season. Spring: the season of spring. Now listen to what the author wants to say: When the last cutting of bersim or garlic was taken, the landowner said to a worker: take care of this bersim and garlic until the seed comes, and whatever seed will be will be shared between us, then without stating duration this contract is valid because just as fruit has a known ripening time, similarly bersim and garlic have a known time for seed, so stating duration is not a condition. And the matter of cultivation is opposite because in cultivation the beginning varies greatly, and when the beginning varies, the end also necessarily varies, so here the duration would be ignorant, therefore stating duration is a condition in agriculture. Note: We have stated earlier that in our region the beginning and end of cultivation are known, so fatwa is given on the validity of muzara'ah without stating duration.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses the condition of duration (mudda) in the musaqah contract. The author begins by presenting the legal conflict between qiyas (analogical reasoning) and istihsan (juristic preference). By qiyas, musaqah is analogous to a lease (ijarah) and to muzara'ah (sharecropping), both of which require a specified duration to avoid uncertainty (gharar). However, by istihsan, musaqah is valid even without stating a duration because the ripening time of fruit is generally known and varies little, unlike crops in muzara'ah. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is istihsan. The passage then applies this principle to bersim (alfalfa) and garlic: when the last crop has been taken and the owner contracts with a worker to tend the plants until seed harvest, no duration need be specified because the seed maturation time is known (like fruit). This is contrasted with regular agriculture (muzara'ah) where planting times vary greatly (autumn, spring, etc.), leading to uncertainty about the end, thus requiring a fixed duration. A concluding note explains that in the commentator's region, the agricultural cycle is well-known, allowing fatwa on the validity of muzara'ah without a stated duration. The commentary thus clarifies the Hanafi ijtihad in balancing qiyas and istihsan for different types of vegetation.

Key Terms
مساقات (musāqāh): A contract where the owner of fruit trees gives them to another to tend and water in exchange for a share of the fruit.
مدت (mudda): The specified period of time for which a contract is valid.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning that would require duration in musaqah by analogy to ijarah.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that permits musaqah without a fixed duration because fruit ripening time is known and uniform.
رطبة (ruṭba): A type of fodder crop, specifically bersim (alfalfa) or a similar plant that is cut multiple times and has a known seed maturation time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is musaqah without a specified duration valid by istihsan?
A) Because the fruit ripening time is unknown, so no condition is needed.
B) Because the contract is a gift, not a lease.
C) Because fruit ripening has a known time and varies little, avoiding uncertainty.
D) Because the parties can terminate the contract at any time.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan allows musaqah without a fixed duration because fruit ripening times are known, making uncertainty negligible.

Exceptions in Musaqah: Trees Not Yet Fruiting and Perennial Roots
Two exceptions requiring duration in musaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two cases where musaqah contracts require a stated duration and explain the legal reason (jahalah fahishah, indefinite growth).

Core Idea
Contracts for care of non-fruiting trees or perennial roots are invalid unless a fixed term is specified.

You have learned that musaqah contracts for mature fruit trees can be made without specifying a duration. However, Imam al-Hidayah presents two important exceptions: when the tree has not yet fruited, and when the plants are perennial roots like date palms or bersim. The ruling changes because the uncertainty (jahalah) becomes excessive, making the contract fasid. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exceptional cases
Read the passage and list the two types of plants for which the contract is invalid without a stated duration: (1) a tree that has taken root but not yet fruited (ghars), and (2) date palms or roots of rutba (bersim) that grow indefinitely.
Focus on the textual markers: 'بخلاف ما اذا دفع اليه غرسا' and 'بخلاف ما اذا دفع نخيلا او اصول رطبة'.
2
Determine the ruling for each case
For both cases, the contract is ruled fasid (voidable) if no duration is stated. It can be corrected by adding a fixed term. Note the difference: for ghars, duration is needed because fruiting time varies grossly; for nakhil/rutba, it is needed because there is no natural end.
Fasid means the contract is defective but can be rectified, unlike batil which is void ab initio.
3
Analyze the legal cause (illah) for invalidity
The illah is jahalah fahishah (gross ignorance) about the time when fruit will appear or when the contract will end. For ghars, soil quality makes the fruiting period uncertain (e.g., 2 vs. 7 years). For roots, they keep growing indefinitely, so the term is completely unknown. This uncertainty invalidates the contract under Hanafi fiqh.
The passage uses the term 'تفاوت فاحش' (extreme variation) and 'لا نهاية معلومة' (no known end).
4
Distinguish from the default rule
In a standard musaqah for mature fruit trees, the end of the harvest season or natural fruiting cycle provides a known endpoint, so no specific duration is required. These exceptions arise when that endpoint is either highly variable or non-existent.
This distinction is key to applying the ruling correctly.
5
Reflect on the cross-madhhab perspective
The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih. The Shafi'i school, for example, generally requires a fixed term in all musaqah contracts to avoid any uncertainty. Recognize that this difference stems from different thresholds for tolerable ignorance (jahalah).
Understanding ikhtilaf strengthens your legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پودا لگایا اور بطور حفاظت و خدمت اس شرط پر دوسرے کے حوالے کر دیا کہ اس کا پھل دونوں کے درمیان نصف نصف ہوگا، حکم
و بخلاف ما اذا دفع اليه غرسا قد علق ولم يبلغ الثمر معاملة حيث لا يجوز الا ببيان المدة لانه يتفاوت بقوة الاراضى وضعفها تفاوتا فاحشا
ترجمہ اور بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ عامل کو پورا دیا جو جم گیا اور پھل دینے کی حد کو نہیں پہنچا بطور معاملہ کے دیا اس حیثیت سے کہ یہ جائز نہیں مگر مدت کو بیان کرنے کے ساتھ اسلئے کہ یہ متفاوت ہوتا ہے تفاوت فاحش کے ساتھ زمینوں کی قوت اور ضعف کے اعتبار سے۔ تشریح ایک شخص نے ایک پودا لگایا اور اس کو دوسرے کے حوالہ کر دیا کہ وہ اس کی حفاظت وخدمت کرے اور اس سے جو پھل ہو گا وہ دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا۔ تو یہ عقد فاسد ہے۔ کیونکہ بعض زمین طاقتور ہوتی ہے کہ اس میں اگر یہ پودا لگایا جا تا تو دو سال میں پھل دے دے گا اور بعض کمزور ہوتی ہیں کہ اس میں سات سال میں پھل آئے گا۔ تو بغیر بیان مدت کے اس میں جہالت فاحشہ ہے اسلئے بیان مدت کے بغیر یہ عقد فاسد ہو گا۔
عاقل سے کہا برسیم کی جڑوں کی حفاظت کر، یہاں تک کہ ان کی اگان ختم ہو جائے تو یہ معاملہ فاسد ہے صورت مذکورہ اور پہلی صورت میں وجہ فرق
وبخلاف ما اذا دفع نخيلا او اصول رطبة على ان يقوم عليها اواطلق فى الرطبة تفسد المعاملة لانه ليس لذالك نهاية معلومة لانها تنمو ما تركت في الأرض فجهلت المدة
ترجمہ اور بخلاف اس کے جبکہ کھجور کا درخت دیا یا برسیم کی جڑیں اس شرط پر کہ وہ ان کی حفاظت کرے یا برسیم میں مطلق بولا تو معاملہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اسلئے کہ اس کے لئے اس کے لئے نہایت معلومہ نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ یہ ( برسیم ) بڑھتی رہے گی جب تک کہ زمین میں چھوڑی
A tree was planted and handed over to another for care and service on condition that its fruit be half-half between them – ruling. And contrary to when he gives him a tree that has taken root but has not yet reached fruiting as a transaction, it is not valid except with stating the duration because it varies greatly according to the strength and weakness of the land. Translation: And contrary to the case when the worker is given a tree that has become firm and has not reached the stage of giving fruit as a transaction, it is not valid except with stating the duration because it varies with great variation according to the strength and weakness of lands. Commentary: A person planted a tree and handed it over to another that he should care for and serve it, and whatever fruit results will be half-half between them. So this contract is void. Because some lands are strong such that if this tree were planted there, it would give fruit in two years, and some are weak such that it would give fruit in seven years. So without stating duration, there is gross ignorance, therefore without stating duration this contract is void. From the contractor he said: take care of the roots of bersim until their growth ends, then this transaction is void – the difference between the mentioned case and the first case. And contrary to when he gives date palms or roots of rutba on condition that he care for them, or he speaks absolutely in rutba, the transaction becomes invalid because there is no known end for it, because it (bersim) keeps growing as long as it is left in the ground, so the duration becomes unknown.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage from the commentary provides two exceptions to the general rule that musaqah contracts can be without a stated duration. The first case: a tree that has been planted (ghars) but has not yet fruited is handed over for care in exchange for a share of future fruit. Such a contract is invalid (fasid) unless a duration is specified. The reason is that the time until fruiting varies grossly (tafawut fahish) depending on soil quality – e.g., two years in strong soil vs. seven in weak soil. This extreme uncertainty (jahalah fahishah) invalidates the contract if no fixed term is set. The second case: date palms (nakhil) or roots of rutba (bersim) are given for care without a specified end, or the contract is simply 'absolute' regarding the rutba. This is invalid because the roots continue to grow indefinitely as long as they are left in the ground, so there is no known endpoint, leading to total uncertainty about the contract's termination. The commentary highlights the legal distinction: where the maturation or end is known and uniform, duration is not required; where it is unknown or varies excessively, duration is necessary to avoid gharar.

Key Terms
غرس (ghars): A tree that has been planted and taken root but has not yet reached fruiting age.
عقد فاسد (ʿaqd fāsid): A voidable contract; it is not valid in its current state but can be made valid by removing the deficiency (e.g., specifying duration).
جہالت فاحشہ (jahālat fāḥishah): Gross ignorance or uncertainty that makes a contract invalid; here, the extreme variation in fruiting time.
نخيل (nakhīl): Date palms, which are perennial and have no definite end to their productivity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a contract invalid when a tree that has not yet fruited is given for care without specifying a duration?
A) Because the tree is too young to produce fruit.
B) Because the time to fruiting varies greatly with soil quality, causing gross uncertainty.
C) Because the worker cannot be trusted.
D) Because the owner must always set a duration for any contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi muamalat, contracts for care of non-fruiting trees or perennial roots require a fixed term to avoid the gross uncertainty (jahalah fahishah) that would otherwise render them fasid.

Berseem and Garlic Contract Without Duration
Qiyas-based ruling on agricultural contract duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a contract for delivering seed of berseem or garlic is valid without a fixed duration, and distinguish it from ordinary cultivation contracts.

Core Idea
When the end of a contract is customarily known, explicit duration is unnecessary.

This passage from the Masaqat chapter addresses a common agricultural scenario: a landowner asks a worker to tend berseem or garlic until the seed harvest, sharing the seed. The Hanafi ruling is that no fixed duration is needed because everyone knows when seed time arrives. We will unpack the analogy (qiyas) with fruit ripening and the contrast with ordinary cultivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its terms
The landowner says: 'Protect this berseem and garlic until the seed comes, and share the seed.' Note that no duration is specified.
2
State the ruling
The contract is valid (ja'iz/sahih) without specifying duration. This is the Hanafi position.
3
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The ruling is based on qiyas jaliy: fruit trees have a known ripening time, so contracts for them need no duration. Similarly, berseem and garlic have a known seed time.
asl (fruit trees) → known time; far' (berseem/garlic) → known time; illa (known end time).
4
Distinguish ordinary cultivation
In ordinary cultivation (zira'ah), the beginning varies greatly (e.g., depending on rain), so the end is also ambiguous. Hence duration is required.
Contrast: here the end is customarily fixed, so no ambiguity.
5
Consider the regional fatwa note
The author adds that in his region, even cultivation timings are known, so fatwa allows muzara'ah without duration.
This shows the role of 'urf (custom) in determining the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المساقاة
بر تیم [؟] یا لہسن کی جب آخری لورہ [؟] گئی تو زمین والے نے کسی عامل سے کہا کہ تم اس برسیم ولہسن کی حفاظت کرو یہاں تک بیج آ جائے اور جو بیچ ہو گا وہ ہمارے اور تمہارے درمیان مشترک ہو گا تو بیان مدت کے بغیر یہ عقد جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ جس طرح پھلوں کے پکنے کا معلوم وقت ہے ایسے ہی برسیم اور لہسن کے بیج کے وقت معلوم ہے اسلئے بیان مدت کی شرط نہ ہو گی۔ اور کھیتی کا مسئلہ اس کے خلاف ہے، کیونکہ کھیتی میں تو ابتداء میں اختلاف کثیر ہوتا ہے اور جب ابتداء میں اختلاف ہو اور انتہاء میں بھی اختلاف ضرور ہوگا۔ تو یہاں مدت مجبول ہوگی اسلئے زراعت میں بیان مدت شرط ہے۔
تنبیه ماقبل میں ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ ہمارے دیار میں کھیتی کی ابتداء اور انتہا معلوم ہے لہذا بیان مدت کے بغیر مزارعت کے جواز پر فتویٰ ہوگا۔
Book of Masaqat. When the last crop of berseem or garlic was taken, the landowner told a worker: 'Protect this berseem and garlic until the seed comes, and whatever seed comes will be shared between us.' So this contract is valid without specifying duration. Because just as the ripening time of fruits is known, similarly the seed time of berseem and garlic is known, therefore specifying duration is not a condition. And the case of cultivation is contrary to this, because in cultivation there is great variation at the beginning, and when there is variation at the beginning, there will necessarily be variation at the end. So there duration is ambiguous, therefore specifying duration is a condition in cultivation. Note: We have mentioned earlier that in our region the beginning and end of cultivation are known, so fatwa is given on the validity of muzara'ah without specifying duration.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Masaqat (irrigation/agricultural contract) chapter. It states that when a landowner gives berseem (clover) or garlic to a worker to tend until the seed is produced, with a share of the seed, the contract is valid even without specifying a duration. The reasoning is analogical (qiyas): just as fruit trees have a known ripening time, these crops have a known seed time. In contrast, ordinary cultivation (kheti/zira'ah) has wide variation in growth duration, so specification is required. A note adds that in the author's region, cultivation also has known timings, so fatwa allows it without duration.

Key Terms
برسیم (barsīm): Egyptian clover (berseem), a fodder crop which has a known seed harvest time.
مزارعت (muzāra‘ah): Cultivation contract where owner provides land and worker provides labor, sharing the crop.
عرف (‘urf): Custom that is widely known and accepted, used to determine the illa in qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the contract for berseem and garlic valid without specifying duration according to this passage?
A) Because these crops do not need protection
B) Because their seed time is customarily known, like fruit ripening
C) Because the worker is a family member
D) Because the share was unspecified

Key Takeaway
When a contract's end is customarily known, explicit duration is not required; this is derived via qiyas on fruit ripening and distinguishes ordinary variable cultivation.

Invalidity of a Young Tree Contract Without Duration
Rules on giving a tree that has not yet fruited for share of fruit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a contract for an unfruited tree without a specified duration and explain why it is fasid due to jahalah fahishah.

Core Idea
A contract for an unfruited tree is fasid without duration because the time to bear fruit is too uncertain.

This passage addresses a specific type of agricultural partnership: giving a sapling that has taken root but not yet fruited to a worker in exchange for a share of the future fruit. The Hanafi school holds that such a contract is invalid unless the duration of the arrangement is clearly stated. The reason is the extreme uncertainty (jahalah fahishah) about when the tree will fruit, which can vary from two to seven years depending on soil quality. Let's walk through the ruling and its justification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a contract (mu'amalah) where a 'ghars' (young tree) is handed over to another person to tend, with the fruit to be shared equally. The ruling is fasid (invalid) unless the duration is specified.
Fasid means the contract is defective; it may be rectified by adding the missing condition.
2
Locate the condition for validity
The condition required is the specification of a duration (muddah). Without it, the contract is invalid.
Duration is needed because the fruiting time is unknown.
3
Understand the cause of invalidity
The cause is jahalah fahishah (excessive ignorance). The time it takes for the tree to fruit varies dramatically between strong and weak land, e.g., two years vs. seven years, creating extreme uncertainty about when the partnership ends.
This is not a minor uncertainty; it is fahish (excessive).
4
Apply the qiyas (analogical reasoning)
The asl (original case) is any contract with jahalah fahishah in a material term, which is fasid. The far' (new case) is this tree contract. The illa (effective cause) is the excessive uncertainty about the fruiting time.
The Hanafi school relies on qiyas jaliy here, comparing to other contracts where excessive ignorance voids the agreement.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) might allow such a contract if the share is specified and the tree is known, but the Hanafi school insists on duration because of the extreme variation.
The practical difference: Hanafi requires a clear end date; others may focus on the share percentage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و بخلاف ما اذا دفع اليه غرسا قد علق ولم يبلغ الثمر معاملة حيث لا يجوز الا ببيان المدة لانه يتفاوت بقوة الاراضى وضعفها تفاوتا فاحشا
ترجمہ اور بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ عامل کو پورا دیا جو جم گیا اور پھل دینے کی حد کو نہیں پہنچا بطور معاملہ کے دیا اس حیثیت سے کہ یہ جائز نہیں مگر مدت کو بیان کرنے کے ساتھ اسلئے کہ یہ متفاوت ہوتا ہے تفاوت فاحش کے ساتھ زمینوں کی قوت اور ضعف کے اعتبار سے۔ تشریح ایک شخص نے ایک پودا لگایا اور اس کو دوسرے کے حوالہ کر دیا کہ وہ اس کی حفاظت وخدمت کرے اور اس سے جو پھل ہو گا وہ دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا۔ تو یہ عقد فاسد ہے۔ کیونکہ بعض زمین طاقتور ہوتی ہے کہ اس میں اگر یہ پودا لگایا جا تا تو دو سال میں پھل دے دے گا اور بعض کمزور ہوتی ہیں کہ اس میں سات سال میں پھل آئے گا۔ تو بغیر بیان مدت کے اس میں جہالت فاحشہ ہے اسلئے بیان مدت کے بغیر یہ عقد فاسد ہو گا۔
And contrary is the case when he gives him a sapling that has taken root but not yet reached fruiting, as a mu'amalah (contract), for it is not permissible except with specification of duration, because it varies greatly according to the strength and weakness of the lands. Translation: And contrary to the case when he gave the worker a plant that had rooted and not reached the limit of giving fruit, as a mu'amalah, such that it is not permissible except with statement of duration, because it varies with great variation according to the power and weakness of lands. Elaboration: A person planted a sapling and handed it to another to protect and serve, and the fruit would be half-half between them. So this contract is invalid (fasid). Because some land is strong, in which if this sapling were planted, it would give fruit in two years, and some are weak, in which fruit will come in seven years. So without specifying duration, there is excessive ignorance (jahalah fahishah). Therefore, the contract is invalid without specifying duration.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage distinguishes a different case: when a tree that has already taken root but has not yet borne fruit is given to a worker to tend, in exchange for a share of future fruit. Such a contract is invalid (fasid) unless the duration is specified. The reason is great uncertainty (jahalah fahishah): the time it takes to bear fruit varies drastically depending on soil quality—some land yields in two years, others in seven. This excessive ignorance invalidates the contract. The ruling highlights that the end must be known or specifiable.

Key Terms
غرس (ghars): A young tree or sapling that has taken root but not yet fruited.
جہالت فاحشہ (jahālah fāhishah): Excessive ignorance about a material fact that invalidates a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is the contract for a young unfruited tree invalid without specifying duration?
A) Because the tree might die
B) Because the time to fruit varies greatly with soil quality, causing excessive ignorance
C) Because the worker might not protect it properly
D) Because the share was unspecified

Key Takeaway
A contract for an unfruited tree is fasid unless the duration is specified, due to excessive uncertainty (jahalah fahishah) about when fruit will appear.

Ruling on Contracts for Palm Trees and Wet Roots Without Known Duration
Ruling with proof on fasid contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on contracts for palm trees and wet roots when no duration is specified, and identify the key condition that determines validity.

Core Idea
A contract for growing crops is valid only if the end of work is known; ignorance of duration invalidates.

This passage deals with contracts where a person gives palm trees or wet berseem roots to another to tend, without fixing a time limit. The ruling distinguishes between cases where the end (like fruiting or harvest) is known by custom and where it is unknown. The key principle is that ignorance (jahalah) regarding the duration renders the contract fasid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts in question
The first contract is for the care of palm trees (nakhīl) and the second for wet berseem roots (uṣūl raṭbah). Both are given to a worker to tend, without a specified end date.
The word اصول رطبة refers to the roots of berseem that continue to grow.
2
Understand the basis for invalidity
The reason given in the text is that there is no known end because wet roots keep growing as long as they remain in the ground, making the duration unknown (majhūl). This jahalah in a condition of the contract renders it fasid.
Jahalah in the duration of work invalidates the contract because it leads to uncertainty (gharar) in compensation.
3
Compare with the earlier valid case
Earlier in the text (not shown here), a contract for berseem roots given until the seed is obtained was valid because the time of seed acquisition is known. Here, the condition is open-ended (e.g., 'until the roots stop growing'), which has no known end.
The distinction is purely based on knowledge of the endpoint, not on the type of crop.
4
Identify the condition for validity
The passage concludes that if the end is known by custom (e.g., time of fruiting or cutting), the contract is valid even without explicit duration. If unknown, it is invalid. This is the muftā bihī position.
The principle is summarized by al-Kasānī: validity depends on knowledge of the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبخلاف ما اذا دفع نخيلا او اصول رطبة على ان يقوم عليها اواطلق فى الرطبة تفسد المعاملة لانه ليس لذالك نهاية معلومة لانها تنمو ما تركت في الأرض فجهلت المدة
ترجمہ اور بخلاف اس کے جبکہ کھجور کا درخت دیا یا برسیم کی جڑیں اس شرط پر کہ وہ ان کی حفاظت کرے یا برسیم میں مطلق بولا تو معاملہ فاسد ہو جائے گا اسلئے کہ اس کے لئے اس کے لئے نهایت معلومہ نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ یہ ( برسیم ) بڑھتی رہے گی جب تک کہ زمین میں چھوڑی جائے گی تو مدت مجہول ہوگئی ۔
تشریح پہلے مسئلہ میں برسیم کی جڑ میں جنس سے مراد آخری لو ہے دینے کو بیان مدت کے بغیر جائز کہا ہے اور اس کو فاسد کہ رہے ہیں ۔ تو فرق یہ ہے کہ پہلے پیج کے حاصل ہونے تک دیا تھا اور اس کا وقت معلوم ہے۔ اور یہاں مراد یہ ہے کہ جب تک حفاظت کرے کہ اس کی جڑوں کی اگان ختم ہو جائے بلکہ جڑیں خشک ہو جائے تو خشک ہونے کی اور اگان کی مدت معلوم نہیں بلکہ زمین میں وہ جب تک رہے گی اگان جاری رہے گا اور سوکھنا متحقق نہ ہو گا تو مدت مجہول ہے اسلئے بغیر بیان مدت کے یہ معاملہ جائز نہ ہوگا یا اس سے اگان ختم ہونے گی اور سوکھنے کی شرط نہیں لگائی بلکہ مطلقاً آخری لو دے دی تو بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ عقد فاسد ہے۔
مگر یہ دلیل جو بیان کی گئی ہے صرف اصول رطبہ میں جاری ہو سکتی ہے بخیل میں نہیں اس وجہ سے بعض شراح نے کہا ہے کہ مصنف نے تخیل کی دلیل بیان نہیں فرمائی جیسا کہ صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا ہے۔
مذکورہ دلیل دونوں کی ہو سکتی ہے اور مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ کھجور کا درخت دے دیا اور کہا کہ اسکی حفاظت کرو اور یہ عقد ہمارے اور تمہارے درمیان جب تک رہے گا جب تک کہ یہ کھجور سوکھ نہ جائے تو یہ عقد فاسد ہے اسلئے کہ اس کی مدت مجہول ہے البتہ اگر خیل میں مطلقا کہا اور سو کھنے وغیرہ کی شرط انہیں لگائی تو عقد صحیح ہوگا اور حسب سابق پہلے پھلوں پر یہ عقد واقع ہو گا مگر برسیم ولہسن کے اندر اطلاق کی صورت میں بھی فساد ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں نہایت معلومہ نہیں ہے۔
تنبیہ ۔ پہلی اور دوسری صورت میں فرق کا مدار نہایت کے علم وعدم علم پر ہے وہاں نہایت معلوم ہے تو اس کو جائز کہا ہے اور یہاں نہایت معلوم نہیں اسلئے اس کو فاسد کہا لہذا اگر اس نے کھجور کے درخت یا برسیم عامل کے حوالہ کی اور اسے حتى تذهب اصولها کی شرط نہیں لگائی اور پھل کے آنے اور بیچ کے آنے کا وقت معلوم ہے تو یہ عقد جائز ہے اور اگر بیچ کے آنے کا وقت معلوم نہ ہو تو پھر عقد فاسد ہوگا۔ شامی ص ۱۸۳ ج ۵۔ مگر انہوں نے پہلی لو آنے پر عقد کو واقع کیا ہے نیز ملاحظہ ہو مجمع الا نہر ص ۴۸۶ ج ۲ ۔
تنبیہ - علامہ کا سائی فرماتے ہیں ولو دفع ارضاً ليزرع فيها الرطاب او دفع ارضا فيها اصول رطبة ثابتة و لم يسم المدة فان كان شيئاً ليس لابتداء نباته ولا لانتهاء جذه وقت معلوم فالمعاملة فاسدة وان كان وقت جذه معلوماً يجوز و يقع على الجذةِ الاولى كما في الشجرة المثمرة - (بدائع ص ١٨٦ ج ٢)
یہ عبارت بالکل صاف ہے کہ جواز و عدم جواز کامدار نہایت کے علم وعدم علم پر ہے خلاصہ کلام صاحب ہدایہ کا کلام صاف نہیں بلکہ کلام میں الجھاؤ ہے بدائع کی عبارت بالکل واضح ہے۔
شیوع کے طریقے پر ایک جز کو متعین کرنا شرط ہے
ويشترط تسمية الجزء مشاعـالـمـا بينا في المزارعة الشرط جزء مـعـيـن يـقـطـع الشركة
And contrary to when he gives palm trees or wet roots (usul ratba) on condition that he tend them, or he speaks absolutely in the case of wet roots, the transaction becomes invalid, because there is no known end for that, because it (berseem) keeps growing as long as it is left in the earth, so the duration is unknown. Translation: Contrary to when palm trees are given or berseem roots on condition that he protect them, or he speaks absolutely regarding berseem, the transaction becomes invalid because there is no known end, because berseem keeps growing as long as it is left in the earth, so the duration is unknown. Elaboration: In the first issue, the reference to the last crop of berseem roots was valid without specifying duration, but here it is said invalid. The difference is that in the first, it was given until the seed is obtained, and its time is known. Here, it means to protect until the roots stop growing or dry up, which is unknown. So without duration, it is invalid. If he gives absolutely, same ruling. But this evidence applies only to wet roots, not to palm trees. Some commentators say the author did not provide evidence for palm trees. The evidence can apply to both, meaning: if he gives a palm tree and says protect until it dries, the contract is invalid because duration unknown. However, if he says absolutely without condition of drying, the contract is valid and applies to first fruits, but for berseem/garlic, even absolute is invalid because no known end. Note: The difference between the first and second case depends on knowledge of the end. If the end is known, it is valid; if unknown, invalid. So if he gives palm tree or berseem to the worker without the condition 'until the roots disappear', and the time of fruit or seed coming is known, the contract is valid; if the seed time is unknown, invalid. Shami p.183 v.5. Note: Allamah Kasani says: 'If he gives land to sow wet roots or gives land containing fixed wet roots and does not name the duration, if it is something whose beginning of plant and end of cutting has no known time, the transaction is invalid; if the time of cutting is known, it is valid and applies to the first cutting, as in the case of a fruit-bearing tree.' (Badai' p.186 v.2). This statement is absolutely clear: validity depends on knowledge of the end. The summary of the author of Hidayah is unclear, but Badai' is clear. And it is a condition to specify the share as common (musha'), as we explained in muzara'ah: the condition is a specified share that ends the partnership.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This lengthy passage clarifies the conditions for contracts involving palm trees and wet roots (berseem roots). The general principle: if the end (niha'yah) is known, the contract is valid without specifying duration; if unknown, it is invalid. The text contrasts the earlier valid case (berseem given until seed time) with this new case where the end is not known (roots keep growing). It also discusses a nuance: the evidence given only applies to wet roots, but some commentators extend it to palm trees. A quote from Badai' al-Sanai' (by Kasani) explicitly states that the ruling depends on knowledge of the cutting time. Finally, a condition for validity: the share must be specified as a common fraction (musha'), just as in muzara'ah, to avoid partnership ambiguity. The passage resolves confusion in the Hidayah author's wording by citing Kasani's clear position.

Key Terms
نخیل (nakhīl): Palm trees (date palms).
اصول رطبہ (uṣūl raṭbah): Wet roots of berseem (clover) that continue to grow.
جذّہ (jaddah): Cutting or harvesting (of wet plants).
مشاع (mushā‘): A common (undivided) share in a property or crop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines whether a contract for berseem roots is valid without specifying duration?
A) The type of soil
B) Whether the end (e.g., cutting time) is known
C) Whether the worker is a Muslim
D) The amount of rain

Key Takeaway
A contract to tend palm trees or wet roots is valid only if the end of the work is known, either by explicit agreement or by custom; otherwise it is fasid.

Distinguishing Palm and Wet Roots: Knowledge of the End and the Condition of Musha'
Expansion and clarification of the ruling's evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why some Hanafi commentators confine the given reason to wet roots and identify the requirement that the share be specified as a common (musha') portion.

Core Idea
The evidence of unknown duration applies directly to wet roots; for palm trees, validity depends on the known time of fruiting — and the share must be musha'.

This lesson builds on the previous by exploring a subtle intra-madhhab discussion: the stated evidence (continuous growth) fits wet roots perfectly, but does it also apply to palm trees? The author of Hidayah has been criticized for not providing separate evidence. Additionally, the passage ends with a crucial condition: the worker's share must be specified as a common fraction (musha'), not a specific plot or plant, to avoid partnership ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the commentator's critique
The passage notes that some scholars (like the author of 'Inayah) said the evidence that 'it keeps growing' applies only to wet roots, not to palm trees, because palm trees are not continually growing in the same way. The author of Hidayah did not give a separate reason for palm trees.
This critique is about the clarity of the proof, not the ruling itself.
2
Apply the general principle to both
The commentary then resolves the issue: the evidence can apply to both if we understand the condition as 'until the fruit dries' — which also has no fixed end unless specified. Alternatively, if no condition is stated, the palm tree contract is valid because the fruit time is known. Thus, the principle is universal: knowledge of the end governs.
This is the mufta bihi position from Badai'.
3
Identify the condition of musha' share
At the end, the passage adds that a condition for validity is that the share be specified as musha' (a common, undivided fraction) rather than a specific part, as in muzara'ah. This prevents the share from becoming a separate ownership that could break the partnership.
The Arabic says: ويشترط تسمية الجزء مشاعاً كما بينا في المزارعة.

Source Text

According to the passage, the evidence that 'it keeps growing' (continuous growth) was explicitly stated in the text for which type of contract?

Death of the Worker in Musaqat: Heirs' Succession and Landowner's Options
Ruling on worker's death in musaqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the heirs' obligation to continue the musaqat contract after the worker's death and explain the landowner's three options when the heirs intend to harvest unripe fruit.

Core Idea
In musaqat, the worker's heirs automatically succeed him—as long as they continue caring for the trees, the contract endures.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in musaqat (orchard partnership): the death of the worker (āmil). The Hanafi school rules that the worker's heirs step into his role and must continue tending the trees, even if the landowner objects. This ruling is based on the principle of mutual benefit (maslahah). However, if the heirs wish to harvest the fruit prematurely while it is unripe, the landowner is given protective options to prevent loss. Understanding this ruling clarifies how Hanafi fiqh balances continuity of contracts with protection against harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its addressees
The passage states that when the worker dies, his heirs (ورثته) are obligated to take care of the trees. Determine who is obliged: the heirs, not the landowner. The heir's obligation is wājib because it is a right of the landowner and a benefit to both parties.
The Arabic phrase 'فلورثته ان يقوموا عليه' clearly places the duty on the heirs.
2
Analyze the rational proof (maslahah)
The reason given is 'li-anna fīhi al-naẓar min al-jānibayn' (because there is regard for both sides). Identify that this is a maslahah-based proof: the continuity benefits the heirs (who get a share of the fruit) and the landowner (who gets his land cared for). This is a rational (aqli) proof, not a text-based one.
Hanafīs often use maslahah as a basis for rulings in mu‘āmalāt, as long as it does not contradict a clear text.
3
Recognize the conditional scenario and its consequence
The passage adds a condition: if the heirs intend to harvest the fruit while it is still unripe (yabsuran), the landowner may suffer loss. In that case, the landowner has three options (khiyārāt) which were previously explained in the text. Identify that this condition modifies the landowner's rights and prevents injustice.
The three options are not repeated here; they refer to earlier material. Typically, the options are: (1) let the fruit ripen and then divide, (2) take the fruit and pay the heirs' share in cash, or (3) cancel the contract and compensate the heirs.
4
Consider the legal effect and cross-madhhab perspective
Understand that the Hanafi position gives the heirs an automatic right to continue, overriding the landowner's personal preference. Some other schools (e.g., Shāfi‘ī) might allow the landowner to refuse the heirs if he has valid grounds, but Hanafīs prioritize the mutual benefit. Note this as a thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
This ikhtilaf stems from different weights given to the consent of the landowner vs. the general principle of maslahah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عامل فوت ہو جائے تو عامل کے ورثہ اس کے قائم مقام ہیں
ولومات العامل فلورثته ان يقوموا عليه وان كره رب الارض لان فيه النظر من الجانبين ترجمہ اور اگر عامل مرجائے تو عامل کے ورثہ کو چاہئے کہ وہ اس کی دیکھ بھال کرتے رہیں اگر چہ زمین والا اس کو نا پسند کرے اسلئے کہ اس میں جانین کیلئے شفقت ہے۔ تشریح عامل کے مرنے کے بعد اس کے ورثہ پھلوں کی دیکھ بھال کریں گے۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں ورثہ عامل اور رب الارض دونوں کا فائدہ ہے۔
ورثاء عامل کو کچا پھل توڑنے کی اجازت مل جائے تو رب الارض کا نقصان ہے لہذ از میندار کو تین اختیارات ملیں گے
فان ارادوا ان يصرموه يسراً كان صاحب الأرض بين الخيارات الثلثة التي بياها ترجمہ پس اگر عامل کے ورثہ نے پھلوں کے کچے توڑنے کا ارادہ کیا تو مالک زمین تین خیارات کے درمیان ہو گا جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح اسلئے کہ اگر در شہ عامل کو کچا توڑنے کی اجازت مل جائے تو رب الارض کا نقصان ہے اسلئے کہ وہی تین اختیارات مالک زمین کو ملیں گے جن کا بار باذکر کیا جا چکا ہے۔
And if the worker dies, his heirs must take care of the trees even if the landowner dislikes it, because there is regard for both sides. Translation: If the worker dies, his heirs should continue caring for it, even if the landowner dislikes it, because there is kindness for both. Commentary: After the worker's death, his heirs will care for the fruit, because there is benefit for both the worker's heirs and the landowner. If the worker's heirs are allowed to pick unripe fruit, the landowner suffers loss; therefore, the landowner has three options. Then if they intend to pick it while unripe, the landowner will have the three options which we have explained. Commentary: Because if the worker is allowed to pick unripe fruit, the landowner suffers loss; therefore, the same three options are given to the landowner as previously mentioned.

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the death of the worker ('āmil) in a musāqāt (orchard partnership) contract. The passage is a ruling with proof, where the proof is rational (maṣlaḥah). The matn states that when the worker dies, his heirs take his place in caring for the trees, even if the landowner (rabb al-arḍ) dislikes it. The reason given is that this arrangement benefits both parties (li-anna fīhi al-naẓar min al-jānibayn). The sharḥ explains this as consideration for both sides. If the heirs wish to harvest the fruit while it is still unripe (yabsuran), this would cause loss to the landowner, so he is given three options (detailed in earlier text): to take the fruit at the current share, to pay the heirs' share in cash, or to let it ripen and then settle. This ruling ensures justice and prevents harm to the landowner.

Key Terms
عامل (āmil): The worker or cultivator in a musāqāt or muzāraʿah contract.
رب الارض (rabb al-arḍ): The landowner or tree owner in a musāqāt partnership.
خیار (khiyār): Option or choice; here, the landowner's three options when the fruit is picked unripe.
نظر (naẓar): Regard, consideration, or benefit; used here to indicate mutual benefit.

The Worker's Heirs' Option in Musaqat: Inheritance or Succession?
Ruling with proof and resolution of a potential objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between inheriting an option (khiyar) and succeeding in a financial right (haqq mali), and explain why the worker's heirs receive the option in musaqat.

Core Idea
The worker's heirs succeed to a financial right, not the option itself.

In Hanafi fiqh, options (khiyar) are considered 'arad (accidents) and are not inheritable. Yet in musaqat, when both parties die, the worker's heirs are given the choice to continue or abandon. This passage resolves the apparent contradiction by explaining that the heirs stand in the worker's place regarding a financial right—the right to keep fruit on trees until ripening—which is a property-related right, not an option as such.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Both the worker (factor) and landowner (rabb al-ard) die during a musaqat contract. Determine what happens to the option to continue or abandon.
2
State the ruling
The option (khiyar) goes to the worker's heirs; they may choose to continue or leave the contract.
3
Recognize the apparent problem
Recall that khiyar is an 'arad (accident) and generally not inheritable. How can it pass to heirs?
This is a common point of confusion in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The text explains this is not inheritance of the option itself, but succession (khilafah) in a financial right (haqq mali). That financial right is the right to leave fruit on trees until ripening.
Thus the heirs act as deputies in a financial right, not as inheritors of an option.
5
Apply the distinction
If the worker's heirs choose to abandon, the landowner's heirs then acquire the three options. This preserves the principle that options as 'arad are not inherited, but financial rights can transfer by succession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر عامل اور رب الارض دونوں مرجائیں تو عامل کے ورثہ قائم مقام ہوں گے
وان ماتا جميعا فالخيار لورثة العامل لقيامهم مقامه وهذا خلافة في حق مالى وهو ترك الثمار على الاشجار على وقت الادراك لا ان يكون وارثة في الخيار ترجمہ اور اگر وہ دونوں مرجائیں تو خیار عامل کے ورثہ کو ہے ان کے عامل کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہ حق مالی میں خلافت ہے اور وہ حق مالی درختوں پر پھلوں کو چھوڑنا ہے پکنے کے وقت تک یہ بات نہیں ہے کہ یہ خیار میں وراثت ہو۔ تشریح اگر عامل اور رب الارض دونوں مرجائیں تو عامل کے ورثہ کو خیار ہے کہ وہ بدستور کام کریں اور یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ کام چھوڑ دین جب یہ کام چھوڑنے کو اختیار کریں گے تو رب الارض کے دورثہ کو ہی مذکورہ تینوں خیارات ملیں گے۔
سوال .. آپ تو ہر جگہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خیار چونکہ عرض ہے اسلئے وہ میراث میں تقسیم نہیں ہوتا۔ حالانکہ یہاں عامل کا خیار آپ نے اس کے ورثہ کو میراث دے کر فرمایا کہ ورثہ عامل کو اختیار ہے تو یہاں یہ اختیار میراث میں کیسے مل گیا ؟
جواب یہ وراثت میں ملا ہوا خیار نہیں ہے بلکہ حق مالی میں وارث مورث کا قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔ احوال تقسیم ترکہ اس کے شاہد ہیں اور وہ حق مالی پکنے تک پھلوں کو درختوں پر چھوڑنا ہے تو ورثہ ایک مالی حق میں مورث کے نائب اور قائم مقام ہوتے ہیں خیاران کو میراث میں نہیں ملا۔
And if both die, the option (khiyar) is for the worker's heirs because they stand in his place, and this is a succession (khilafah) in a financial right, which is to leave the fruit on the trees until they ripen, not that they inherit the option. Translation: If both die, the option goes to the worker's heirs due to their standing in his place, and this is a succession in a financial right, and that financial right is to leave the fruit on the trees until the time of ripening; it is not that they inherit the option. Commentary: If both the worker and landowner die, the worker's heirs have the option to continue the work or to leave it. If they choose to leave it, then the landowner's heirs will have the three options mentioned. Question: You always say that khiyar is an accident ('arad) and therefore not divided in inheritance. Yet here you give the worker's option to his heirs by way of inheritance. How is this? Answer: This is not an inherited option; rather, the heir stands in the place of the deceased in a financial right. The circumstances of dividing the estate prove this. That financial right is to leave the fruit on the trees until they ripen. So the heirs are deputies in a financial right, not inheritors of the option.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where both the worker and the landowner die. It clarifies that the choice (khiyar) to continue or abandon the musāqāt goes to the worker's heirs because they succeed him in a financial right (ḥaqq mālī). Specifically, the right to keep the fruit on the trees until ripening is a financial right, distinct from the option (khiyār) as an accident ('araḍ). The author includes a question addressing a potential confusion: since option is generally not inheritable (being an accident), how can it pass to heirs? The answer explains that this is not inheritance of the option itself, but the heirs standing in the worker's place regarding a financial right. Thus, when the worker's heirs choose to stop, the landowner's heirs then acquire the three options. This reasoning preserves the principle that options as such are not inherited, while financial rights (like possession) can transfer by succession.

Key Terms
خلافت في حق مالي (khilāfah fī ḥaqq mālī): Succession in a financial right, where the heir stands in the deceased's place concerning property-related entitlements.
عرض (ʿaraḍ): An accident; a non-permanent attribute that cannot be inherited according to Hanafīs.

D) The judge awards it to them

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khiyar passes to heirs not as inheritance but as succession in a financial right, preserving the rule that options themselves are not inherited.

Ruling When Worker's Heirs Refuse to Continue in Musaqat
Ruling when the worker's heirs decline to take over the care of trees.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the worker's heirs refuse to continue the musaqat contract and identify the three options available to the landowner's heirs.

Core Idea
If the worker's heirs abandon the orchard, the landowner's heirs inherit the same three options the landowner had.

In a musaqat contract, if the worker dies and his heirs refuse to care for the trees, the landowner's interests must be protected. The Hanafi school rules that the landowner's heirs gain the same rights (khiyar) that the original landowner had. This lesson explains that transfer and the available choices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
Recognize that the worker's death and his heirs' refusal to continue the work (qiyam) activates the transfer.
2
Recognize the transfer of khiyar
The option (khiyar) passes to the landowner's heirs, not to a third party.
This prevents the orchard from being neglected.
3
Recall the three options
The landowner's heirs can: (1) take the fruit as is, (2) pay the worker's share, or (3) let the fruit ripen.
These are the same options the landowner had.
4
Apply the ruling
In a hypothetical scenario, determine which option the landowner's heirs might choose and why.
Consider factors like fruit ripeness and financial advantage.

Ruling on Expiry of Mu'amalah: Musaqat vs Muzara'ah When Crop Is Unripe
Ruling with proof comparing musaqat and muzara'ah after contract expiry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling for musaqat and muzara'ah when the contract period ends with unripe produce, and explain the underlying illah based on the permissibility of leasing.

Core Idea
After contract expiry with unripe fruit, the worker in musaqat works unpaid because trees cannot be leased; in muzara'ah, he pays land rent and shares work.

In musaqat and muzara'ah, if the contract period ends before the harvest, the worker still has unfinished work. The Hanafi school treats the two contracts differently based on the nature of the underlying asset: trees vs. land. This lesson examines the reasoning (ta'lil) behind the divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contracts
Define musaqat (sharecropping on trees for fruit) and muzara'ah (sharecropping on land for crops). Understand the typical arrangement: the worker tends the trees/land and receives a share of produce.
2
State the common scenario
The contract period expires while the fruit or crop is still unripe (busr akhdar). The produce is not yet ready for harvest. What is the worker's obligation?
3
Extract the ruling for musaqat
The worker must continue to care for the trees without any additional wage (lā yajūz istījāruh). All work falls on the worker alone because trees cannot be leased.
This is the key difference from muzara'ah.
4
Extract the ruling for muzara'ah
The worker pays the landowner the rental equivalent (ujrat al-mithl) for the land, and then the work of cultivation after the period is shared between both parties.
Land can be leased, so a rental value can be assessed.
5
Identify the illah and apply qiyas
The effective cause (illah) is the permissibility of leasing the asset: trees cannot be leased, land can. Thus, in musaqat (the far'), the worker must work without wage, analogously to the principle that if no rental is payable, the worker bears all work (as in the original contract). In muzara'ah (the asl), the land can be leased, so after expiry the worker pays rent and work is shared.
This is a qiyas khafi because the illah is extracted via tahqīq al-manāṭ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مزارعت کی مدت ختم ہو جائے اور کھیتی کچی ہو تو عامل کو اپنے حصہ کی اجرت دینی پڑے گی اور کام دونوں پر ہو گا
قال واذا انقضت مدة المعاملة والخارج بسر اخضر فهذا والاول سواء وللعامل ان يقوم عليها الى ان يدرك لكن بغير اجر لان الشجر لا يجوز استيجاره بخلاف المزارعة في هذا لان الارض يجوز استيجارها و كذالك العمل كله على العامل ههنا وفى المزارعة فى هذا عليهما لانه لما وجب اجر مثل الارض بعد انتهاء المدة على العامل لا يستحق عليه العمل وههنا لا اجر فجاز ان يستحق العمل كما يستحق قبل انتهائها
He said: And when the period of the mu'amalah ends and the produce is unripe and green, then this and the first are the same. The worker has the right to tend it until it ripens, but without wage, because trees cannot be leased. Unlike muzara'ah in this respect, because land can be leased. And likewise all the work here (in musaqat) is on the worker, while in muzara'ah in this case it is on both of them, because when the land's rental equivalent becomes due from the worker after the period ends, work is not due from him, but here there is no wage, so it is permissible that work be due from him just as it was due before the period ended.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage provides a comparative ruling between musāqāt and muzāraʿah when the contract period expires and the crop/fruit is still unripe. In musāqāt, the worker must continue to care for the trees without any additional wage until the fruit ripens, because trees cannot be leased (ujrat) — i.e., you cannot rent a tree for its fruit. Therefore, all work falls on the worker alone. In contrast, in muzāraʿah (sharecropping on land), after the period ends, the worker must pay the landowner the rental equivalent (ujrat al-mithl) for the land, but then the work of cultivation after that is shared between both parties. The reason is that land can be leased, so a rental value can be assessed. Since the worker here (in musāqāt) does not pay rent, he must perform all work himself without wage. The passage thus highlights the underlying illah (effective cause): the permissibility of leasing the asset (land vs. trees).

Key Terms
اجر مثل الارض (ujrat mithl al-arḍ): The rental equivalent of the land; what it would cost to rent similar land.
استیجار (istījār): Leasing or renting; here, the act of leasing trees or land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must the worker in musāqāt tend the trees without additional wage after the contract period ends, unlike in muzāraʿah?
A) Because the worker is obligated by the original contract
B) Because trees cannot be leased, so no rental payment is owed
C) Because the fruit belongs to the landowner
D) Because the landowner compensates the worker later

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the post-expiry treatment of musaqat and muzara'ah turns on whether the underlying asset can be leased; since trees cannot be leased, the worker in musaqat must continue without pay, while in muzara'ah land rent is paid and work is shared.
