Valid Excuses for Cancelling a Musaqat Contract
Listing excuses for faskh of musaqat with reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi excuses for cancelling a musaqat contract and apply the principle that harm not undertaken justifies faskh.

Core Idea
A musaqat contract may be cancelled if the worker is a thief or too ill, because these harms were not agreed.

In this passage, the author of Al-Hidayah lists the valid excuses that allow either party to cancel a musaqat contract. The reasoning is based on qiyas to ijara: if a harm arises that was not undertaken in the contract, the affected party may terminate. Two specific excuses are given, and a third is debated within the school. Understanding these excuses is crucial for determining when a musaqat agreement remains binding and when it can be dissolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its analogy
The passage begins by stating that musaqat is cancelled due to excuses, as previously explained in ijara. Identify that the basis is qiyas: the same harm-based reasoning from hire contracts applies here.
The text says 'لما بينا فى الاجازات' (as we explained in ijara).
2
List the two main excuses
Extract the two clear excuses: (1) the worker is a thief feared to steal fruit or branches; (2) the worker becomes too ill to work personally. For each, note the harm: the owner suffers loss in (1), the worker suffers additional burden in (2).
Both harms were not undertaken in the original contract.
3
Analyze the reasoning for each excuse
For the thief: the owner faces harm (theft) that he did not agree to bear. For illness: requiring the worker to hire replacements at his own expense imposes hardship not stipulated. In both cases, cancellation is justified to prevent unagreed harm.
This is the core of the Hanafi approach: harm not undertaken allows faskh.
4
Examine the internal ikhtilaf on voluntary abandonment
The passage notes two narrations regarding whether the worker voluntarily leaving the work is an excuse. Read the interpretation: one narration says it is an excuse only if personal work was stipulated; otherwise not. Understand the qualification.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference, not a dispute with other schools.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Based on the commentator's clarification, the relied-upon position is that leaving work is not an excuse unless the contract expressly required the worker's personal labour. If the worker could delegate, it is not an excuse.
The second narration is preferred because it avoids unnecessary disruption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتفسخ بالأعذار لما بينا فى الاجازات وقد بينا وجوه العذر فيها ومن جملتها ان يكون العامل سارقاً يخاف عليه سرقة السعف والثمر قبل الادراك لانه يلزم صاحب الارض ضرر لم يلتزمه فيفسخ به ومنها مرض العامل اذا كان يضعفه عن العمل لان فى الزامه استيجار الاجراء زيادة ضرر عليه ولم يلتزمه فيجعل ذالك عذرا ولو اراد العامل ترک ذالك العمل هل يكون عذرا فيه روايتان وتاويل إحدهما ان يشترط العمل بيده فيكون عذرا من جهته تشريح مزارعت کے اندر اگر مدت ختم ہو جائے اور کھیتی کچی ہو تو عامل کو اپنے حصہ کی اجرت دینی پڑتی ہے اور کام دونوں پر ہوتا ہے لیکن اگر مساقات میں یہ صورت ہو جائے تو عامل پر اجرت نہ ہوگی کیونکہ درختوں کا اجارہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور جب عامل کے اوپر اجرت واجب نہیں تو رب الارض کے ذمہ کام نہ ہوگا بلکہ عامل بدستور کام کرتارہے گا جیسے مدت کے ختم ہونے سے پہلے کرتا رہا ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام ۔ جہاں عامل پر اجرت نہیں ہے وہاں کام اسی کے ذمہ ہے اور جہاں اجرت ہے وہاں کام دونوں پر ہو گا تنہا عامل پر نہ ہوگا۔ سوال عامل یہ تو کر سکتا ہے کہ مزدوروں سے کام کر دے پھر عذر کہاں ؟ جواب ... عقد میں اس نے اس کا التزام نہیں کیا تھا تو یہ اس پر ضر ر ڈالنا ہوگا۔ ولو اراد.... الخ - عامل نے اپنی لائن ہی بدلنے کا ارادہ کر لیا تو کیا اس کو عذر شمار کیا جائے گا۔ تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ عذر نہیں اور عامل پر کام کیلئے جبر ہوگا۔ اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ عذر شمار کیا جائے گا لیکن اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہ طے ہوا ہو کہ عامل اپنے ہاتھ سے کام کرے گا تب یہ عذر شمار ہو گا ورنہ دوسروں کے ذریعہ کام کر سکتا ہے تو پھر یہ عذر شمار نہ ہوگا۔
He said: It (musaqat) is cancelled due to excuses as we explained in ijaraat. And we have explained the aspects of excuse therein. Among them: that the worker is a thief, it is feared that he will steal the unripe fruit and branches before ripening, because it causes harm to the owner which he did not undertake, so it is cancelled by it. And among them: the worker's illness if it weakens him from work, because obliging him to hire workers is additional harm upon him which he did not undertake, so that is considered an excuse. And if the worker intends to leave that work, is that an excuse? There are two narrations. The interpretation of one: that work by his hand is stipulated, then it is an excuse from his side. Commentary: In muzara'ah, if the period ends and the crop is unripe, the worker must pay hire for his share and the work is upon both. But in musaqat, if this situation occurs, there is no hire on the worker because leasing trees is not permissible. When hire is not obligatory on the worker, the work is not upon the owner; rather the worker continues working as before. Summary: Where there is no hire on the worker, work is upon him alone; where there is hire, work is upon both, not solely on the worker. Question: The worker can get others to do the work, so where is the excuse? Answer: He did not undertake that in the contract, so it would be imposing harm on him. And if he intends to change his line... there are two narrations: one says it is not an excuse and the worker is compelled to work; the other says it is an excuse but only if it was stipulated that he work with his own hand; otherwise he can work through others and it is not an excuse.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the excuses that allow cancellation of a musaqat contract. The matn states that musaqat is cancelled due to excuses, as previously explained in the chapter on ijara. The commentator then specifies two main excuses: (1) the worker is a thief who might steal unripe fruit or branches, causing harm the owner did not undertake; (2) the worker becomes ill to the extent that he cannot work, because forcing him to hire replacements would cause him additional hardship not agreed upon. The passage also discusses whether the worker voluntarily leaving the work is an excuse. There are two narrations: in one it is not an excuse; in the other it is, but only if the contract required him to work personally. The Urdu commentary clarifies the difference between muzara'ah and musaqat regarding the end of the term: in muzara'ah, if the crop is unripe, the worker must pay hire for his share and both parties work; in musaqat, no hire is due because trees cannot be leased, so the worker continues working alone. The commentary also addresses the question that the worker could hire others, explaining that he did not undertake that, so forcing him would be harm.

Key Terms
مساقات (musāqāt): A contract where the owner of fruit trees gives them to a worker to tend in exchange for a share of the fruit.
فسخ (faskh): Cancellation or rescission of a contract, here due to valid excuses.
عذر (ʿudhr): A valid excuse that permits cancellation of the contract, such as theft or illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a worker in a musaqat contract becomes too ill to work personally, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The contract is automatically void.
B) The contract may be cancelled because illness is an excuse.
C) The worker must hire a replacement at his own expense.
D) The owner must hire a replacement.

Key Takeaway
A musaqat contract can be cancelled when a harm arises that was not part of the original agreement, such as the worker being a thief or becoming incapacitated.

Invalidity of Planting Trees on Condition of Half-Share
Ruling on giving barren land for planting with half-share condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a planting contract with a half-share condition and apply the analogy to qafiz al-tahhan to determine its validity.

Core Idea
A contract to plant trees on another's land with half-ownership stipulation is fasid due to pre-existing partnership and qafiz al-tahhan analogy.

This lesson examines a specific planting contract where a landowner gives barren land to a planter for a fixed period, on condition that both the land and the trees become half-owned by each. The Hanafi school rules this contract invalid. Let's explore the reasoning behind this ruling and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract terms
The landowner provides barren land; the planter agrees to plant trees for a fixed number of years. They stipulate that after planting, both land and trees will be owned equally.
Note the condition of half-share in the land itself, which predates the work.
2
Spot the invalid condition
The condition creates partnership in something that already existed before the partnership (the land). Partnership is for acquiring future assets, not for already-owned property.
3
Apply the qiyas to qafiz al-tahhan
This contract resembles the prohibited 'qafiz al-tahhan' where a miller is paid with a portion of the flour he grinds—hiring for an uncertain portion of the output. Here, the planter is hired for a share of the garden (land and trees) that includes pre-existing property.
The analogy is based on the common element of hiring for an uncertain share of the produce.
4
Determine the consequences
The contract is fasid (corrupt). The planter does not receive the stipulated half-share. Instead, he gets the value of the plants he planted and a customary wage for his labor, because the plants are attached and cannot be returned.
The landowner retains full ownership of the land and trees.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من دفع ارضا بيضاء الى رجل سنين معلومة يغرس فيها شجر اعلى ان تكون الارض والشجر بين رب الأرض والغارس نصفين لم يجز ذالك لاشتراط الشركة فيما كان حاصلا قبل الشركة لا بعمله وجميع الثمر والغرس لرب الارض وللغارس قيمة غرسه وأجر مثله فيما عمل لانه في معنى قفيز الطحان اذ هو استيجار ببعض ما يخرج من عمله وهو نصف البستان فيفسد وتعذر رد الغراس لا تصالها بالارض فيجب قیمتها واجر مثله لانه لا يدخل في قيمة الغراس لتقومها بنفسها وفى تخريجها طريق اخر بيناه في كفاية المنتهى وهذا اصحهما والله اعلم . تشريح شرکت کا مقصد یہ ہوتا ہے کہ جو چیز ابھی حاصل نہیں ہے اس کو حاصل کیا جائے او پہلے سے حاصل شدہ چیز کیلئے شرکت نہیں ہوا کرتی اور کہیں ایسی صورت سامنے آ جائے تو عقد کو فاسد کہا جائے گا۔ ما قبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ تفیز الطحان نا جائز ہے جس کا ثبوت نص سے ہے تو وہ چیز جو فیز لاطحان کے درجہ میں آئے گی اس کو بھی فاسد کہا جائے گا جب یہ تفصیلات ذہن نشین ہو گئیں تو اب سنئے کہ مالک زمین نے ایک شخص کو چند معلوم سالوں کے لئے اپنی زمین دے دی کہ دوسرا اس میں درخت لگائے پھر زمین اور درخت صاحب ارض اور عامل (غارس) کے درمیان آدھے آدھے ہو جائیں گے تو یہ صورت جائز نہیں ہے کیوں؟
And whoever gives barren land to a man for known years to plant trees in it on condition that the land and trees be half between the landowner and the planter, it is not permissible because of stipulating partnership in what was obtained before the partnership, not by his work. And all the fruit and planting belong to the landowner, and the planter has the value of his planting and the hire of his labor, because it is in the meaning of qafiz al-tahhan, as it is hiring for a portion of what comes from his work, which is half the garden, so it becomes corrupt. And returning the plants is difficult due to their connection to the land, so their value must be paid along with the hire of his labor, because it is not included in the value of the plants as they are valuable in themselves. And there is another way of extraction which we explained in Kifayat al-Muntaha, and this is the more correct of the two, and Allah knows best. Commentary: The purpose of partnership is to obtain what is not yet obtained, and partnership does not occur in something already obtained. If such a situation arises, the contract is said to be corrupt. It has passed previously that qafiz al-tahhan is impermissible, proven by text, so anything that falls into the category of qafiz al-tahhan will also be declared corrupt. Now that these details are understood, listen: The landowner gave his land to a person for several known years that he should plant trees in it, then the land and trees become half between the landowner and the worker (planter). This situation is not permissible. Why?
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the invalidity of a specific planting contract. It addresses a scenario where a landowner gives barren land to a person for a fixed number of years to plant trees, on condition that the land and the trees become joint property between them half and half. The ruling is that this contract is not permissible (ghayr ja'iz). The reason given is that it stipulates partnership in something that already exists before the partnership (the land) and not solely from the worker's labor. The worker is entitled to the value of the plants he planted and the customary wage for his labor, because the contract is analogous to the prohibited 'qafiz al-tahhan' (a contract where a miller is paid with a portion of the flour he grinds), which is a form of hiring for an uncertain portion of the output. Since the plants are attached to the land and cannot be removed, they are valued, and the worker also gets a separate wage for his work. The commentator notes that there is another way of deriving this ruling, mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha, but the given ruling is the more correct one. The Urdu commentary elaborates that partnership is meant for acquiring something not yet acquired, not for something already owned. The prohibition is based on analogy to qafiz al-tahhan, which is established by textual evidence (hadith).

Key Terms
قفيز الطحان (qafīz al-ṭaḥḥān): A prohibited hiring contract where a miller is paid with a specific measure (qafiz) of the flour he grinds; used as an analogy for invalid sharecropping arrangements.
غارس (ghāris): The person who plants trees; the worker in this planting contract.
شركة (shirkah): Partnership; here it refers to joint ownership of land and trees which is invalidly stipulated in a pre-existing property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a landowner gives his land to a planter with the condition that after planting, the land and trees will be half-owned by each, what does the planter receive according to the Hanafi ruling?
A) Half of the land and trees as stipulated.
B) Nothing because the contract is void.
C) The value of the plants he planted and a wage for his labor.
D) Only the value of the plants.

Key Takeaway
A planting contract that conditions half-ownership of both land and trees is fasid; the planter is compensated with the value of his plants and a wage, not the stipulated share.

Ruling on Slaughter by Muslims and People of the Book
Ruling with proof from Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for lawful slaughter and explain why the uncircumcised and circumcised are equal.

Core Idea
The lawfulness of meat depends on the slaughterer's faith and skill, not on circumcision or political status.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes the Hanafi ruling on slaughter by Muslims and People of the Book. It clarifies that the permissibility is rooted in the Quranic verse (5:5) and depends on three specific qualities in the slaughterer. Understanding these conditions is essential for determining halal meat in diverse scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
The passage states that slaughter by a Muslim or Kitabi is halal (permissible). The proof is the Quranic verse (5:5): 'And the food of those who were given the Scripture is lawful for you.' The word 'food' is interpreted as slaughtered meat.
2
Isolate the three conditions
The slaughterer must: 1) know the tasmiya (saying Bismillah), 2) know the correct place to cut the throat, 3) be skilled in cutting the veins. These are conditions (shurut) for the slaughter to be valid.
Even if the slaughterer is a child, insane, or woman, the conditions still apply.
3
Understand the scope of the slaughterer
The slaughterer can be male or female, child or insane—as long as they possess the three qualities. The key is intentionality: they must be capable of performing the slaughter with intent.
4
Resolve the circumcision issue
The passage explicitly says that the uncircumcised (aqlaf) and circumcised (makhtun) are equal. The criterion is faith (Islam or Kitabi status), not physical circumcision.
Some might think circumcision is required, but Hanafi law rejects that.
5
Define Kitabi inclusively
The term Kitabi includes all People of the Book: dhimmi, harbi, Arab, non-Arab. The condition is the existence of a millah of tawhid, whether in belief or by claim.
This means even a Kitabi from a non-Muslim state (harbi) is included.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الذبائح
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مسلمان اور کتابی کا ذبیحہ حلال ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم تلاوت کر چکے ہیں اور اللہ تعال کے فرمان ( اور ان لوگوں کا کھانا جو کتاب دیئے گئے ہیں تمہارے حلال ہے) کی وجہ سے اور ذبیحہ حلال ہوگا جبکہ ذابح تسمیہ کو سمجھتا ہو اور ذبیح کرنے کو جانتا ہو۔ اور [؟] اوراج کاٹنے پر ضابط ہو اگر چہ بچہ ہو یا مجنون یا عورت بہر حال جب کہ وہ ضابط نہ ہو اور نہ تسمیہ اور ذبح کو سمجھتا ہو تو حلال نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ نص کی وجہ سے ذبیحہ پر تسمیہ شرط ہے اور یہ قصد سے ہوگا اور ارادہ کی صحت ان چیزوں سے ہوگی جس کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اور اقلف ( غیر مختون) اور مختون دونوں برابر ہیں اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اور کتابی کا اطلاق کتابی ذمی اور حربی اور عربی اور تعلیمی کا شامل ہے اسلئے کہ شرط ملت کا قیام ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو گذر گئی ہے۔
تشریح مسلمان اور کتابی کا ذبیحہ حلال ہے ماقبل میں ذکر کردہ دلیل سے اور آیت میں طعام سے ذبیحہ مراد ہے۔ ذبح کرنے والا مرد ہو یا عورت بچہ ہو یا مجنوں سب جائز ہے بس یہ بات ضروری ہے کہ ذائج اپنے اندر تین اوصاف رکھتا ہو۔
ا تسمیہ جانتا ہو۔
-۲- مقام ذبح سے واقف ہو۔
- [؟] جورگیں ذبح میں کائی جاتی ہیں ان سے واقف ہو۔
کیونکہ اگر یہ صفات نہ ہوں گی تو با اقصد تسمیہ پر کیسے قادر ہو گا۔ حالانکہ نص سے ذبیحہ پر تسمیہ کہنا شرط ہے اقلف اور مختون برابر ہیں کیونکہ مدار ختنہ ہونے یا نہ ہونے پر نہیں ہے بلکہ اسلام یا کستانی ہونے پر ہے۔ (کمامز ) مدارختنہ پھر کتابی میں ہر قسم کا کتابی مراد ہے دار السلام کا باشند د ہو یا دارالحرب کا، عربی ہو یا تعلمی وغیرہ۔ کیونکہ اصل شرط ہے تو ملت تو حید کا قیام ہے خواہ اعتقاد ا ہو یا بطور دعوی کے۔
Book of Slaughter. Translation: Quduri said: The slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi is lawful due to the proof we have recited and due to Allah's command (And the food of those who were given the Scripture is lawful for you). And the slaughtered animal will be lawful when the slaughterer understands the tasmiya and knows how to slaughter, and is skilled at cutting the veins, even if he is a child, an insane person, or a woman. In any case, if he is not skilled and does not understand tasmiya and slaughter, it will not be lawful. Because by the text, tasmiya is a condition for slaughter, and this is done with intention, and the validity of intention depends on what we have mentioned. And the uncircumcised and the circumcised are equal due to the proof we have mentioned. And the term Kitabi includes the dhimmi, the harbi, the Arab, and the non-Arab, because the condition is the existence of the millah, according to the details that have passed. Commentary: The slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi is lawful from the proof mentioned earlier, and in the verse, 'food' means slaughtered meat. The slaughterer may be male or female, child or insane—all are permissible. It is only necessary that the slaughterer possesses three qualities: 1. He knows the tasmiya. 2. He is aware of the place of slaughter. 3. He knows the veins that are cut in slaughter. Because if these qualities are not present, how can he be capable of intentionally performing tasmiya? Whereas by the text, saying tasmiya over the slaughter is a condition. The uncircumcised and circumcised are equal because the criterion is not being circumcised or not, but rather being Muslim or Kitabi. Then, for the Kitabi, every type of Kitabi is meant, whether a resident of Dar al-Salam or Dar al-Harb, Arab or non-Arab, etc. Because the fundamental condition is the existence of the millah of tawhid, whether in belief or by claim.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and Sunnah. It states that the slaughter of a Muslim or a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) is halal (permissible). The proof is the Quranic verse (5:5) where 'food' is interpreted as slaughtered meat. Three conditions are required for the slaughterer: knowledge of tasmiya (saying Bismillah), knowledge of the correct place to cut (the throat), and skill in cutting the veins. Even if the slaughterer is a child, insane, or woman, as long as they meet these conditions, the slaughter is valid. The uncircumcised (aqlaf) and circumcised (makhtun) are equal because the criterion is faith, not circumcision. The term 'Kitabi' includes all People of the Book, whether dhimmi or harbi, Arab or non-Arab, as long as they adhere to a millah (religion) that believes in tawhid, even if only by claim.

Key Terms
تسمیہ (tasmiya): Uttering 'Bismillah' (in the name of Allah) at the time of slaughter.
ضابط (dabit): One who is skilled and knowledgeable in the proper method of slaughter, including cutting the veins.
اقلف (aqlaf): An uncircumcised man.
مختون (makhtun): A circumcised man.
ملت (millah): A religious community or creed; here it refers to the religion of tawhid (monotheism).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the slaughter of an uncircumcised (aqlaf) Muslim?
A) It is haram because circumcision is required.
B) It is halal, same as a circumcised Muslim.
C) It is makruh tanzihi.
D) It is only permissible if he repents and gets circumcised.

Key Takeaway
Slaughter is halal when the slaughterer, whether Muslim or Kitabi, meets the three conditions of knowing tasmiya, knowing the place, and being skilled at cutting; circumcision and political status are irrelevant.

Ruling on the Slaughter of a Magian (Majusi)
Declares the slaughter of a Magian impermissible with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating Majusi slaughter and cite the hadith proof that distinguishes them from Ahl al-Kitab.

Core Idea
The Magian’s slaughter is haram because he lacks tawhid, as per the Prophet’s command.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling: the meat of an animal slaughtered by a Magian. While Magians are granted aman like the People of the Book, the Prophet ﷺ made two exceptions. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining lawful consumption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the exact act being ruled upon? It is the consumption of meat from an animal slaughtered by a Magian (Zoroastrian). What is the ruling? It is haram (impermissible).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Treat them with the same Sunnah as the People of the Book, except that you do not marry their women, nor eat their slaughtered animals.'
The hadith is a specific prohibition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'nor eat their slaughtered animals.' This is an explicit command to refrain, indicating prohibition. The Hanafi principle is that such an explicit command yields haram.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that Magians are treated like Ahl al-Kitab in all respects, including the permissibility of their slaughter. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the hadith's two exceptions.
This is a legitimate difference of ijtihad.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on this hadith as authoritative and does not override it with istihsan. Therefore, the prohibition is the mufta bihi (operative ruling).

Source Text

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مجوسی کا ذ بجہ نہیں کھایا جائے گا حضور 63 کے فرمان کی وجہ سے طریقہ اختیار کرو مجوسی کے ساتھ اہل کتاب کا طریقہ در آنحالیکہ نکاح کرنے والے نہ ہوں ان کی عورتوں سے اور نہ کھانے والے ہوں ان کے ذبیحوں کو اور اسلئے کہ مجوسی توحید کا [؟] مدق نہیں ہے تو ملت معدوم ہو گئی اعتقاد اور دعوی دونوں اعتبار سے۔ تشریح آتش پرست چونکہ تو حید کو کھوئے ہوئے ہے ا: ا اس کا ذبیحہ حلال نہ ہوگا اور اس حدیث سے بھی یہ بات ثابت ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جیسے اہل کتاب کو جہ یہ ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے امان مل جاتا ہے ان کو بھی مل جائے گا۔ فرق یہ ہے کہ اہل کتاب کی عورتوں سے نکاح جائز ہے مجوسی کی عورتوں سے نہیں۔ اور اہل کتنا بکاؤ بچہ حلال ہے مجوسی کا نہیں۔

بحد بیث بایں الفاظ نہیں ملی البتہ یہ مضمون ہے۔ اہل کتاب کو اپنی عورت دینا جائز نہیں صرف ان کی عورتوں سے نکاح کیا جا
He said: The slaughtered animal of a Magian is not to be eaten, because of his saying (peace be upon him): Treat them with the same Sunnah as the People of the Book, except that you do not marry their women, nor eat their slaughtered animals. And because he does not claim tawhid, so the millah is non-existent in belief and claim. Translation: Quduri said: The slaughtered animal of a Magian will not be eaten, due to the command of the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace): Adopt the way with the Magians as with the People of the Book, except that you are not marrying their women and not eating their slaughtered animals. And because the Magian is not a claimant of tawhid, so the millah is extinct in both belief and claim. Commentary: Since the fire-worshipper has lost tawhid, his slaughter will not be halal, and this is proven by this hadith. The gist is that just as the People of the Book are given aman due to paying jizya, they (Magians) are also given aman. The difference is that marrying the women of the People of the Book is permissible, but not Magian women. And the slaughtered animal of the People of the Book is halal, while that of the Magian is not. He can... The hadith in these exact words is not found, but the meaning is this: it is not permissible to give one's daughter to a Kitabi, only marriage with their women is allowed.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from hadith. It states that the slaughter of a Magian (Majusi/Zoroastrian) is not halal. The proof is a hadith commanding that Magians be treated like People of the Book in terms of jizya and protection, but with two exceptions: their women may not be married, and their slaughtered meat may not be eaten. The rationale is that Magians do not believe in or claim tawhid, so they lack the millah of monotheism that is a condition for lawful slaughter. The commentary clarifies that while Magians are given aman (safe conduct) like the Ahl al-Kitab (just as the Ahl al-Kitab are given aman due to paying jizya), the exception regarding marriage and slaughter remains. The text also includes a note that a Kitabi may not give his daughter in marriage to a Muslim, but a Muslim may marry a Kitabi woman.

Key Terms
مجوسی (majusi): A follower of Zoroastrianism, a fire-worshipper.
توحید (tawhid): The belief in the oneness of Allah.

D) Because they do not use the tasmiya.

Key Takeaway
The slaughter of a Magian is haram because the Magian lacks tawhid, as established by the hadith that treats them like Ahl al-Kitab except in marriage and slaughter.

Rulings on Slaughter of Apostates and Idolaters
Explains that slaughter of an apostate and an idolater is not halal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of meat from an animal slaughtered by an apostate or an idolater, and apply the principle of considering the slaughterer's status at the time of slaughter.

Core Idea
An apostate's slaughter is haram; a Kitabi's new religion determines the ruling at slaughter.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a common question: when is the meat of an animal slaughtered by a non-Muslim permissible? The Hanafi school distinguishes between apostates (murtadd) and idolaters (wathani) on one hand, and People of the Book (Kitabi) on the other. The key principle is that the ruling depends on the slaughterer's religious status at the exact moment of slaughter, not their origin or past beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage presents two types of people whose slaughter is not halal: the apostate (murtadd) and the idolater (wathani). Note that a third category, the Kitabi who changes religion, is treated differently.
Apostate = one who left Islam; Idolater = worshipper of idols/multiple gods.
2
Understand the reasoning for each
For the apostate: he has no millah (valid monotheistic religion) because he is not allowed to remain on apostasy. For the idolater: he has no millah at all. For the Kitabi: he is confirmed upon his new religion according to the Hanafi school.
Millah here means a recognized monotheistic religion with a scripture.
3
Apply to a Kitabi convert
If a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) converts to another religion, he is considered to be upon that new religion. Therefore, at the time of slaughter, we look at that new religion to decide if his slaughter is halal.
Examples: Jew becomes Christian → halal; Jew becomes Magian → not halal.
4
Contrast with an apostate
Unlike the Kitabi, an apostate from Islam is never confirmed upon his new religion. Hence his slaughter is always haram, regardless of what he converts to.
This is because an apostate is legally considered to have no religion.
5
State the operative principle
The overarching principle: the ruling is based on the slaughterer's state at the moment of slaughter. For idolaters, it is always haram; for apostates, always haram; for Kitabis, depends on their current millah.
This principle is mufta bihi (relied upon for fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والمرتد لانه لا ملة له فانه لا يقر على ما انتقل اليه بخلاف الكتابى اذا تحول الى غير دينه لانه يقر عليه عندنا فيعتبر ما هو عليه عند ه عند الذبح لا ماقبله قال والوثني لانه لا يعتقد الملة ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور نہیں کھایا جائے گا مرتد کا ذبیحہ اسلئے کہ اسکی کوئی ملت نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ وہ برقرار نہیں رکھا جائے گا اس ملت پر جس کی جانب وہ منتقل ہوا ہے بخلاف کتابی کے جبکہ وہ پھر گیا اپنے دین کے غیر کی جانب اسلئے کہ وہ ہمارے نزدیک اس پر باقی رکھا جائے گا تو اعتبار کیا جائے گا اس حالت کا جس پر وہ بوقت ذبح ہے نہ کہ اس سے پہلے کا قدوری نے فرمایا اور نہیں کھایا جائے گا بت پرست کا ذبیحہ اسلئے کہ وہ ملت کا اعتقاد نہیں رکھتا۔
تشریح مرتد اپنے حال پر باقی نہیں رکھا جائے گا تو اس کا کوئی دین نہیں لہذا اس کا ذبیحہ بھی حلال نہیں ہے البتہ اگر کتابی دوسرا دین اختیار کرے تو اس کو منتقل الیہ پر برقرار رکھا جائے گا۔
اب دیکھا جائے گا کہ بوقت ذبیح وہ کون سی ملت پر ہے اگر ایسی ملت پر ہے جن کا ذبیحہ حلال ہے تو اس کا ذبیحہ حلال ہو گا اور اگر ایسی ملت پر ہے کہ جن کا ذبیحہ حلال نہیں ہے تو اس کا ذبیحہ حلال نہیں ہوگا۔
مثلا ایک یہودی تھا نصرانی ہو گیا تو اس کا ذبیحہ حلال ہے اور اگر مجوسی ہو گیا تو اس کا ذبیحہ حلال نہ ہو گا۔ خلاصہ کلام . بوقت ذبح وہ جس حال پر ہے اس حال کا اعتبار ہو گا۔ بت پرستوں کا ذبیحہ بھی حلال نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کی کوئی ملت نہیں ہے۔
He said: And the apostate (not eaten) because he has no millah, for he is not confirmed upon that to which he has converted, unlike the Kitabi when he changes to a religion other than his own, because he is confirmed upon it with us, so consideration is given to what he is upon at the time of slaughter, not what came before. He said: And the idolater (not eaten) because he does not believe in any millah. Translation: Quduri said: The slaughter of an apostate will not be eaten because he has no millah; he will not be confirmed upon the religion to which he has converted. In contrast, if a Kitabi changes to a different religion, he is confirmed upon it according to us, so consideration is given to his state at the time of slaughter, not before. Quduri said: And the slaughter of an idolater will not be eaten because he does not believe in any millah. Commentary: An apostate is not left upon his state, so he has no religion; therefore his slaughter is not halal. However, if a Kitabi adopts another religion, he is confirmed upon the new one. Now it will be seen which millah he is upon at the time of slaughter. If it is a millah whose slaughter is halal, then his slaughter is halal; if it is a millah whose slaughter is not halal, then his slaughter is not halal. For example, if a Jew becomes a Christian, his slaughter is halal; if he becomes a Magian, his slaughter is not halal. In summary, the state at the time of slaughter is considered. The slaughter of idolaters is also not halal because they have no millah.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling regarding the slaughter of an apostate (murtadd) and an idolater (wathani). An apostate has no valid religion; since he is not left upon his apostasy but rather executed or asked to repent, he has no millah, so his slaughter is haram. For a Kitabi who changes his religion, the ruling depends on his new religion at the time of slaughter. According to the Hanafi school, a Kitabi who changes to another recognized religion (e.g., Jew becomes Christian) is confirmed upon his new religion, so if that religion allows slaughter (i.e., is a monotheistic millah), his slaughter is halal. However, if he becomes a Magian or an idolater, his slaughter is not halal. The general principle is that the state at the time of slaughter is what matters. Idolaters (wathani) have no millah at all, so their slaughter is never halal.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A person who abandons Islam for another religion or unbelief.
وثنی (wathani): An idolater, a worshipper of idols or multiple gods.
ملة (millah): A monotheistic religion with a divine scripture, legally recognized for the validity of slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Jew converts to Christianity and then slaughters an animal, what is the ruling on that meat according to this passage?
A) It is halal because he was originally a Kitabi.
B) It is halal because he is now a Christian, whose slaughter is halal.
C) It is haram because he changed his religion.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
An apostate and an idolater have no valid millah, so their slaughter is haram; a Kitabi's slaughter is judged by his status at the time of slaughter, not his origin, and this determines permissibility.

When is Slaughter Valid: Ruling for Muhrim and Haram
Explains that a muhrim may not slaughter game, and game slaughtered in the Haram is invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a muhrim's slaughter is valid and evaluate the reasoning behind the prohibition of game.

Core Idea
Slaughter of game by a muhrim or in the Haram is invalid because a prohibited act cannot serve as a valid dhabh.

This lesson examines a key fiqh ruling regarding the validity of slaughter (dhabh) when performed by a person in ihram (muhrim) or within the sacred precincts of Makkah (Haram). The central teaching distinguishes between game (hunted animals) and domestic animals, clarifying that only game is affected by these two prohibitions. Through a concise legal reasoning (talil), the text explains why such slaughter is invalid and provides exceptions for non-game animals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios and Their Rulings
The passage gives two distinct cases: (1) a muhrim's slaughter of game, and (2) slaughter of game within the Haram. For both, the meat is not to be eaten (invalid dhabh). Note that the ruling applies equally to muhrim and non-muhrim in the Haram when game is involved.
2
Recognize the Common Element – Game
The prohibition centers on 'game' (sayd), not all animals. In the Haram, the prohibition applies to game regardless of who slaughters; for the muhrim, it applies to game anywhere. Domestic animals (e.g., goat, chicken) are excluded.
Game refers to wild, huntable animals; domestic animals are not game.
3
Understand the Legal Reasoning (Talil)
The reasoning is that dhabh is a 'prescribed act' (mashru'), meaning it is a valid act of worship or legal act only when performed on a permissible subject. Since hunting game is prohibited for a muhrim and within the Haram, the act of slaughtering game in these contexts is itself prohibited, thereby invalidating the dhabh.
The principle: a prohibited action cannot be the means to a valid prescribed act.
4
Apply the Distinction to Non-Game Cases
The passage explicitly contrasts: if a muhrim slaughters non-game (e.g., a goat) anywhere, or if non-game is slaughtered in the Haram by anyone, the dhabh is valid. The Haram does not grant security to domestic animals, and slaughtering them is not prohibited for a muhrim.
Thus, the prohibition is specific to game, not all animals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والمحرم يعنى من الصيد وكذا لايوكل ما ذبح فى الحرم من الصيد والاطلاق في المحرم ينتظم الحل والحرم والذبح في الحرم يستوى فيه الحلال والمحرم وهذا لان الذكاة فعل مشروع وهذا الصنيع محرم فلم تكن ذكاة بخلاف ما اذا ذبح المحرم غير الصيد او ذبح فى الحرم غير الصيد صح لانه فعل مشروع إذ الحرم لا يو من الشاة وكذا لا يحرم ذبحه على المحرم
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور نہیں کھایا جائے گا محرم کا ذبیحہ یعنی شکار میں سے اور ایسے ہی نہیں کھایا جائے گا وہ شکار جس کو حرم میں ذبح کیا گیا ہو اور محرم کے اندر اطلاق حل اور حرم دونوں کو شامل ہے اور ذبح حرم میں اس میں حلال اور محرم دونوں برابر ہیں اور یہ اسلئے کہ ذکاۃ فعل مشروع ہے اور یہ طریقہ حرام ہے تو یہ ذکاۃ نہ ہو گا بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ محرم نے غیر شکار کو ذبح کیا ہو یا حرم میں غیر شکار ذبح کیا گیا ہو تو صحیح ہے اسلئے کہ یہ فعل مشروع ہے اسلئے کہ حرم بکری کو امن نہیں دیتا اور ایسے ہی محرم پر اس کا ذبح حرام نہیں ہے۔
He said: And the muhrim's slaughter (not eaten) meaning of game, and similarly, what is slaughtered in the Haram from game is not eaten. The absolute term 'muhrim' includes both the resident (hal) and the pilgrim (muhrim). And slaughter in the Haram is equal whether it is done by a hal (non-muhrim) or a muhrim. This is because dhabh (slaughter) is a prescribed act, and this action (slaughtering game) is prohibited, so it is not a valid dhabh. Unlike if the muhrim slaughters non-game, or if non-game is slaughtered in the Haram, it is valid because it is a prescribed act. Since the Haram does not grant security to a goat, and similarly, its slaughter is not forbidden for the muhrim. Translation: Quduri said: The slaughter of a muhrim, i.e., from game, will not be eaten. Likewise, game that is slaughtered in the Haram will not be eaten. The term 'muhrim' includes both the hal (non-muhrim) and the muhrim. And slaughter in the Haram applies equally to hal and muhrim. This is because dhabh is a prescribed act, and this act (hunting) is prohibited, so it is not a valid dhabh. In contrast, if a muhrim slaughters non-game, or if non-game is slaughtered in the Haram, it is valid because it is a prescribed act. Since the Haram does not grant security to a goat, and similarly, its slaughter is not forbidden for the muhrim.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the validity of slaughter by a person in ihram (muhrim) and slaughter within the Haram (the sacred precincts of Makkah). A muhrim may not slaughter game (hunted animals) because hunting is prohibited in ihram. Similarly, any game slaughtered within the Haram is invalid, regardless of whether the slaughterer is in ihram or not, because hunting in the Haram is also prohibited. The reasoning is that dhabh is a prescribed act (mashru') that must be performed on a permissible animal. Since the act of slaughtering game in these circumstances is prohibited, it cannot be considered a valid dhabh. However, if a muhrim slaughters a domestic animal (non-game), or if any animal other than game is slaughtered in the Haram, it is valid because the act is not prohibited. The Haram does not provide immunity to domestic animals like goats, and slaughtering them is not forbidden.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct around the Kaaba in Makkah.
ذکاۃ (dhabh): The prescribed method of slaughtering animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person in ihram slaughters a chicken (non-game) in the Haram, what is the ruling on that meat?
A) It is invalid because both conditions are prohibited.
B) It is valid because it is non-game and the Haram does not affect domestic animals.
C) It is valid only if the person is a muhrim.
D) It is invalid because the Haram forbids all slaughter.

Key Takeaway
The validity of dhabh depends on the permissibility of the animal and the act; game is prohibited for muhrim and in the Haram, but domestic animals are not affected.

8 min
Ruling on Slaughter of Apostate and Idol Worshipper
States ruling with reasoning based on milla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the slaughter of an apostate and an idol worshipper and explain the legal reasoning based on the principle of milla.

Core Idea
An apostate and an idol worshipper have no valid milla, so their slaughter is haram.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn, with its commentary, establishes a key principle: the permissibility of dhabah (slaughter) depends on the slaughterer's religious affiliation at the time of slaughter. The ruling distinguishes between an apostate (murtadd) and a Kitabi who changes religion. This lesson unpacks that distinction, helping you understand the Hanafi position on which slaughterers are acceptable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the slaughter (dhabah) performed by an apostate or idol worshipper. The ruling is that it is unlawful (haram) to eat from such slaughter.
2
Understand the key term 'milla'
The ruling hinges on whether the slaughterer has a valid milla (religious community recognized by Islamic law). Only Islam and the Kitabi religions (Judaism, Christianity) are recognized.
3
Apply the principle to the apostate
An apostate leaves Islam and is not confirmed in any new religion (since he adopted a false religion). Therefore, he has no milla, making his slaughter invalid.
4
Contrast with a Kitabi who changes religion
According to Hanafi fiqh, a Kitabi who converts to another Kitabi religion (e.g., Jew becomes Christian) retains his Kitabi status because he is confirmed (muqarr) upon the new religion. His slaughter remains halal if the new religion is a valid milla.
5
Apply to the idol worshipper
An idol worshipper has no revealed scripture and does not believe in any milla, so his slaughter is also invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والمرتد لانه لا ملة له فانه لا يقر على ما انتقل اليه بخلاف الكتابى اذا تحول الى غير دينه لانه يقر عليه عندنا فيعتبر ما هو عليه عند الذبح لا ما قبله قال والوثني لانه لا يعتقد الملة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور نہیں کھایا جائے گا مرتد کا ذبیحہ اسلئے کہ اسکی کوئی ملت نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ وہ برقرار نہیں رکھا جائے گا اس ملت پر جس کی جانب وہ منتقل ہوا ہے بخلاف کتابی کے جبکہ وہ پھر گیا اپنے دین کے غیر کی جانب اسلئے کہ وہ ہمارے نزدیک اس پر باقی رکھا جائے گا تو اعتبار کیا جائے گا اس حالت کا جس پر وہ بوقت ذبح ہے نہ کہ اس سے پہلے کا قدوری نے فرمایا اور نہیں کھایا جائے گا بت پرست کا ذبیحہ اسلئے کہ وہ ملت کا اعتقاد نہیں رکھتا۔
تشریح مرتد اپنے حال پر باقی نہیں رکھا جائے گا تو اس کا کوئی دین نہیں لہذا اس کا ذبیحہ بھی حلال نہیں ہے البتہ اگر کتابی دوسرا دین اختیار کرے تو اس کو منتقل الیہ پر برقرار رکھا جائے گا۔
اب دیکھا جائے گا کہ بوقت ذبیح وہ کون سی ملت پر ہے اگر ایسی ملت پر ہے جن کا ذبیحہ حلال ہے تو اس کا ذبیحہ حلال ہو گا اور اگر ایسی ملت پر ہے کہ جن کا ذبیحہ حلال نہیں ہے تو اس کا ذبیحہ حلال نہیں ہوگا۔
مثلا ایک یہودی تھا نصرانی ہو گیا تو اس کا ذبیحہ حلال ہے اور اگر مجوسی ہو گیا تو اس کا ذبیحہ حلال نہ ہو گا۔ خلاصہ کلام . بوقت ذبح وہ جس حال پر ہے اس حال کا اعتبار ہو گا۔ بت پرستوں کا ذبیحہ بھی حلال نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کی کوئی ملت نہیں ہے۔
He said: And the apostate, because he has no religion, for he is not confirmed on that which he has changed to, unlike the Kitabi when he converts to another religion, because he is confirmed on it with us, so consideration is given to what he is upon at the time of slaughter, not before. He said: And the idol worshipper, because he does not believe in a religion.
Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: The slaughter of an apostate is not eaten because he has no religion, for he will not be retained on the religion to which he has converted, unlike the Kitabi when he turns to another religion, for he is retained on it according to us, so consideration is given to his state at the time of slaughter, not before. Imam al-Quduri said: The slaughter of an idol worshipper is not eaten because he does not believe in a religion.
Explanation: The apostate will not be retained on his state, so he has no religion; therefore his slaughter is not halal. However, if a Kitabi adopts another religion, he is retained on the one he converted to. Now it will be seen at the time of slaughter which religion he is upon: if it is a religion whose slaughter is halal, his slaughter will be halal; if it is a religion whose slaughter is not halal, his slaughter will not be halal. For example, if he was a Jew and became a Christian, his slaughter is halal; if he became a Magian, his slaughter is not halal. Summary: Consideration is given to his state at the time of slaughter. The slaughter of idol worshippers is also not halal because they have no religion.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling from the matn of al-Quduri, commented upon in al-Hidayah. The rule is that the slaughter of an apostate (murtadd) and an idol worshipper (wathani) is unlawful (haram). The reasoning is based on the legal principle that a person's religious affiliation at the time of slaughter determines the permissibility of their slaughter. An apostate has no valid religion accepted by Islamic law, as he is not confirmed on the religion he converted to (since he abandoned Islam). In contrast, if a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) changes his religion, he is still considered a Kitabi according to the Hanafi school, because he is confirmed on the new religion (e.g., if he becomes a Christian from Judaism, his slaughter is still halal because he remains a Kitabi). The determining factor is his status at the moment of slaughter, not his previous religion. The idol worshipper, like the apostate, has no recognized religion, so his slaughter is also unlawful. This ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that the permissibility of dhabah depends on the slaughterer having a valid creed (milla).

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): One who has left the religion of Islam after being a Muslim.
وثني (wathani): Idol worshipper; one who worships idols and has no revealed scripture.
ملة (milla): A religious community or creed recognized by Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Jewish person converts to Christianity, is his slaughter halal according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because he is still a Kitabi.
B) No, because he changed his religion.
C) Yes, but only if he reconverts to Judaism.
D) No, because conversion invalidates all previous rulings.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of dhabah depends on the slaughterer's valid milla at the time of slaughter; an apostate and an idol worshipper lack a valid milla, making their slaughter haram.

Intentional vs Forgetful Omission of Tasmiyah in Slaughter
Presents the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki positions on omitting tasmiyah, with Hanafi evidence from ijma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki positions on omitting tasmiyah and apply the Hanafi ruling based on the distinction between intentional and forgetful omission.

Core Idea
Intentionally omitting tasmiyah makes slaughter haram; forgetting does not. The Hanafi position is upheld by ijma'.

A meat eater's halal status hinges on a single utterance: 'Bismillah'. The three major schools differ sharply on what happens when it is omitted. This lesson unpacks their positions and the Hanafi proof from consensus.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the ruling for intentional omission? For forgetful omission? Cite the matn's key phrase.
From the text: 'If intentionally omitted, it is carrion; if forgetfully, it is eaten.'
2
Identify opposing positions
How does al-Shafi'i rule? How does Malik rule? Note both cases.
Shafi'i: halal in both. Maliki: haram in both.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proofs
What dalil does the passage provide? Focus on the claim of ijma' and the Companion opinions.
Ijma' of earlier scholars on intentional omission; disagreement only on forgetful.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in meat consumption for each school?
Hanafi: intentional = haram; Shafi'i: always halal; Maliki: always haram.
5
Apply the taqliq (expansion) to hunting
The passage extends the dispute to releasing falcons/dogs or shooting arrows. Apply the same distinction.
Intentional omission at time of release makes game haram (Hanafi).

تشریح ذبیحہ پر تسمیہ کہنا ضروری ہے امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر بھول کر یا قصد انتسمیہ چھوڑ دیا ہوتو ذبیحہ حلال نہیں ہوا۔ اور امام شافعی بالکل اس کے برعکس فرماتے ہیں یعنی عمدا چھوڑے یا بھول کر دونوں صورتوں میں ذبیحہ حلال ہے۔ حنفیہ بین بین ہیں وہ فرماتے ہیں اگر بھول کر چھوڑ دے تو ذبیحہ حلال ہے اور اگر عمد ا چھوڑ دے تو ذبیحہ مردار ہے، حرام ہے اس کو کھایا نہیں جائے گا۔ ان حضرات کا یہ اختلاف جیسے مسلمان میں ہے ایسے ہی کتابی میں ہے۔ اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا اور مسلمان اور کتابی ترک تسمیہ میں برابر ہیں۔ کسی نے تیر پھینکتے ہوئے یا شکار پر باز اور کتا چھوڑتے ہوئے تسمیہ چھوڑ دیا۔ اب بھی یہی اختلاف ہے۔ یعنی ہمارے یہاں اگر بھول کر چھوڑ دیا اور شکار پکڑ لیا گیا اس حال میں کہ وہ مرچکا ہے تو حلال ہے۔ اور اگر عمد التسمیہ چھوڑا ہو تو حلال نہیں ۔
امام شافعی کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں حلال ہے۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں حلال نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
اور شافعی کا یہ قول اجتماع کے خلاف ہے اسلئے کہ شافعی سے پہلے لوگوں میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے متروک التسمہ عامداً کی حرمت میں، ان کے درمیان اختلاف بھول کر متروک تسمیہ کے اندر ہے پس ابن عمر کامذہب یہ ہے کہ وہ حرام ہے اور علی ابن عباس کا
He said: And if the slaughterer intentionally omits the tasmiyah, the carcass is carrion, not to be eaten; and if he omits it forgetfully, it is eaten. Al-Shafi'i said: It is eaten in both cases. Malik said: It is not eaten in both cases. The Muslim and the Kitabi are equal in our view regarding omitting tasmiyah. And upon this difference is if one omits tasmiyah when sending the falcon and dogs at the time of shooting.
And this statement of al-Shafi'i is contrary to consensus, for there is no disagreement among those before him regarding the prohibition of intentionally omitting tasmiyah; rather the disagreement among them is about omitting it forgetfully. For the madhhab of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) is that it is prohibited, and the madhhab of Ali and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) is that it is permissible, unlike the intentionally omitted tasmiyah. For this reason, Abu Yusuf and the mashayikh (may Allah have mercy on them) said: There is no room for ijtihad in the case of intentionally omitting tasmiyah; even if a judge gives a verdict permitting its sale, it is not executed because it is against consensus.
Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: If the slaughterer intentionally omits the tasmiyah, the slaughtered animal is carrion, not to be eaten. If he omits it forgetfully, it is eaten. Al-Shafi'i said: It is eaten in both cases. Malik said: It is not eaten in both cases. The Muslim and the Kitabi are equal regarding omitting tasmiyah. And upon this difference is when one omits tasmiyah at the time of releasing the falcon and dogs and at the time of shooting the arrow.
Explanation: Saying tasmiyah over the slaughtered animal is necessary. Imam Malik says that if one omits tasmiyah forgetfully or intentionally, the slaughtered animal is not halal. Imam Shafi'i says exactly the opposite: whether intentional or forgetful, it is halal. The Hanafis are in between: they say if one omits it forgetfully, it is halal; if intentionally, it is carrion, haram, not to be eaten. This difference applies to Muslims and Kitabis alike. The author stated that Muslim and Kitabi are equal in omitting tasmiyah. If someone omits tasmiyah when shooting an arrow or releasing a falcon or dog upon game, the same difference applies. According to us, if he omitted forgetfully and the game is caught dead, it is halal; if intentionally omitted, it is not halal.
According to Imam Shafi'i, it is halal in both cases. According to Imam Malik, it is not halal in both cases. Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint: And this statement of al-Shafi'i is against consensus, for there is no disagreement among those before him regarding the prohibition of intentionally omitting tasmiyah. The disagreement among them is only about omitting it forgetfully. Ibn Umar's madhhab is that it is prohibited; Ali and Ibn Abbas's madhhab is that it is permissible, unlike the intentionally omitted tasmiyah. Therefore, Abu Yusuf and the mashayikh said: There is no room for ijtihad in the case of intentionally omitting tasmiyah; even if a judge gives a verdict permitting its sale, it is not executed because it is against consensus.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage presents a major inter-madhhab dispute regarding the omission of tasmiyah (uttering Bismillah) during slaughter. The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, distinguishes between intentional omission (عمد) and forgetful omission (نسيان). If the slaughterer intentionally leaves out tasmiyah, the meat is carrion (ميتة) and impermissible. If he forgets, it is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that in both cases the meat is permissible. Imam Malik holds it impermissible in both cases. The ruling applies equally to Muslims and People of the Book (Kitabis). The same difference applies when sending a hunting falcon or dog, or shooting an arrow: if tasmiyah is omitted intentionally, the game is not halal; if forgetfully, it is halal. The passage then provides a strong Hanafi argument by citing consensus (ijma'): all scholars before al-Shafi'i agreed on the prohibition of intentionally omitting tasmiyah; the only disagreement was regarding forgetful omission, with some Companions (Ibn Umar) saying it is prohibited and others (Ali, Ibn Abbas) saying it is permissible. Therefore, the Shafi'i position on intentional omission contradicts this consensus. Abu Yusuf and later mashayikh ruled that there is no scope for ijtihad on this point; a judge's verdict permitting its sale would be invalid. This demonstrates the Hanafi reliance on the precedent of the Companions and the principle of ijma'.

Key Terms
تسمية (tasmiyah): Uttering 'Bismillah' (In the name of Allah) before slaughter.
ميتة (maytah): Carrion; an animal that died without proper Islamic slaughter.
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the scholars of the Ummah on a legal ruling.
ذابح (dhabih): The slaughterer; the person performing the ritual slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ibn Umar
B) Ali and Ibn Abbas
C) Abu Bakr
D) Umar

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that intentional omission of tasmiyah makes meat haram based on consensus, while forgetful omission does not.

9 min
Intentional Omission of Tasmiyah: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on intentional omission of tasmiyah in slaughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intentionally omitting tasmiyah, identify the proof from Quran and Sunnah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Intentionally omitting Bismillah makes the meat haram by Quran and consensus; Shafi'is disagree based on a hadith and qiyas.

This lesson examines one of the most practical disputes between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: what happens when a Muslim slaughterer intentionally leaves out saying 'Bismillah'? The Hanafi school, relying on the explicit prohibition in Quran 6:121 and the consensus of the Companions, rules the meat haram. The Shafi'i school, citing a hadith that 'the Muslim slaughters in Allah's name' and a qiyas with wudu, considers it halal. Understanding this difference is crucial for determining which meat is permissible for Hanafis.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school hold regarding intentional omission of tasmiyah? The meat is haram (unlawful).
The Hanafi position is supported by Abu Yusuf and the Mashayikh, who say ijtihad is not possible because it contradicts ijma.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school objects and on what grounds? Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the meat is halal even if the slaughterer intentionally omits tasmiyah.
Shafi'is consider tasmiyah recommended (sunnah) but not a condition.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is the Shafi'i dalil? A hadith: 'The Muslim slaughters in the name of Allah, whether he says tasmiyah or not,' and a rational analogy: if tasmiyah were a condition, it would not be waived due to forgetfulness, but Hanafis waive it in forgetfulness, so it is not a condition.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut this? They present Quran 6:121 (explicit prohibition), ijma of the Sahaba and Tabi'un, and the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim where the Prophet makes prohibition conditional on omission of tasmiyah. The qiyas on wudu is rejected because the analogy is not perfect.
The Hanafi response emphasizes that the Quranic command is clear and the consensus is binding.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of this dispute? A Hanafi Muslim cannot eat meat from an animal slaughtered by a Muslim who intentionally omits tasmiyah, while a Shafi'i Muslim can.
This affects dietary practices and slaughter guidelines for Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الذبائح

مذہب یہ ہے کہ وہ حلال ہے بخلاف عمد متروک التسمیہ کے اور اسی وجہ سے ابو یوسف اور مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ عمد متروک التسمیہ میں اجتہاد کی گنجائش نہیں ہے اور اگر قاضی نے اس کی بیع (متروک التسمیہ عامدا کی بیع) کے جواز کا فیصلہ کیا تو وہ نافذ نہ ہوگا اس فیصلہ کے مخالف اجماع ہونے کی وجہ سے۔

تشریح صحابہ اور تابعین اس پر متفق ہیں کہ جس پر عمدا تسمیہ ترک کر دیا ہو تو وہ حرام ہے۔ البتہ اگر بھول کر چھوڑ دیا ہوتو اس میں اختلاف ہے۔

حضرت ابن عمر اس کو حرام کہتے ہیں۔ اور حضرت علی اور حضرت ابن عباس اس کو حلال کہتے ہیں۔ چونکہ متروک التسمیہ عمداً کی حرمت اجماعی ہے لہذا اس میں اجتہاد بھی نہیں ہو سکتا۔ یعنی یہ مسئلہ مجتہد فیہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اگر قاضی بھی اس کی بیع کے جواز کا فیصلہ کرے تو چونکہ یہ فیصلہ اجماع کے مخالف ہے اسلئے یہ فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ اس تقریر سے یہ معلوم ہوا کہ امام شافعی کا یہ قول اجماع کے خلاف ہے۔ تنبیہ اصول فقہ کی بعض کتابوں میں اور حسامی [؟] ص ۱۵۵ پر اور اس کی شروح میں امام شافعی پر بڑی تشفیع کی گئی ہے اور کہا ہے کہ یہ جہالت عذر شمار نہیں کی جائے گی۔ تو امام شافعی کا عذر یہ ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک اجماع کا ثبوت نہیں ہو سکا اور نہ وہ ہرگز اجتماع کی مخالفت نہیں کر سکتے تھے۔

امام شافعی کی دلیل

له قوله عليه السلام المسلم يذبح على اسم الله تعالى سمى اولم يسم ولان التسمية لو كانت شرطا للحل لما سقطت بعذر النسيان كالطهارة فى باب الصلوة ولو كانت شرطا فالملة اقيمت مقامها كما في ال[؟]

ترجمہ شافعی کی دلیل نبی علیہ السلام کا یہ فرمان ہے کہ مسلمان اللہ کے نام پر ذبح کرتا ہے۔ تسمیہ کہے یا نہ کہے اور اسلئے کہ تسمیہ اگر حالت کی شرط ہوتا تو تسمیہ بھول کے عذر سے ساقط نہ ہوتا جیسے نماز کے باب میں طہارت ہے اور اگر تسمیہ شرط ہو تو ملت تسمیہ کے قائم مقام کر دی جائے کی جیسے ناسی میں ۔ تشریح یہ امام شافعی کی دلیل ہے۔
1 حدیث کہ مسلمان تو اللہ ہی کے نام پر ذبح کرتا ہے خواہ تسمیہ کہے یا نہ کہے حدیث مطلق ہے عمد اور نسیان کی کوئی تفصیل اس میں نہیں ہے۔ -۲ دلیل عقلی۔ اگر آپ تسمیہ کو شرط کہیں گے تو پھر وضو کے درجہ میں ہوگا کہ وضو عمداً چھوڑ دیا سہواً بہر صورت نماز نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اذا فات الشرط فات المشروط قاعدہ کلیہ ہے۔ حالانکہ آپ نسیان کی صورت میں تسمیہ کی وجہ سے ذبیحہ کو حلال کہتے ہیں اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ شرط نہیں اور جب شرط نہیں تو اگر عمدا ترک ہو جائے تو ذبیحہ مردار نہ ہو گا۔ نیز امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر بالفرض تسمیہ کو شرط مان لیں تو جیسے نسیان کی صورت میں ملت توحید تسمیہ کے قائم مقام ہوگئی ہے تو عمداً کی صورت میں بھی ملت توحید تسمیہ کے قائم مقام ہوگی۔

احناف کی دلیل

ولنا الكتاب وهو قوله تعالى ولا تاكلوا مما لم يذكر اسم الله عليه الآية نهى وهو للتحريم والاجماع وهو ما بينا والسنة وهو حديث عدي بن حاتم الطائي رضى الله عنه فانه عليه السلام قال فی آخره فانک انما میت علی کلبک ولم تسـم عـلـی کــلــب غيــرك عـلـل الـحـرمـة بترك التسمية

ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل کتاب ہے اور وہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان ہے اور نہ کھاؤ ان جانوروں میں سے جن پر اللہ کا نام ذکر نہیں کیا گیا، یہ نہی ہے اور یہ تحریم کے لئے ہے اور ہماری دلیل اجماع ہے اور وہ وہ ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور حدیث ہے اور وہ عدی ابن حاتم طائی رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث ہے جس میں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کے آخر میں فرمایا ہے کہ تو نے اپنے کتے پر تسمیہ کہا ہے اور اپنے کتے کے غیر پر تسمیہ نہیں کہا آپ نے حرمت کی علت ترک تسمیہ کو قرار دیا ہے۔

تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے جو تین ہیں۔ کتاب اللہ ارشاد باری ہے ولا تأكلوا مما لم يذكر اسم الله عليه یعنی جن ذبیحوں پر تسمیہ نہیں کہا گیا ان کو مت کھاؤ۔ لا تأكلوا نہی کا صیغہ ہے جو تحریم کیلئے ہے معلوم ہوا کہ متروک التسمیه عمدا کو کھانا حرام ہے۔
1 اجماع امت یعنی امام شافعی سے پہلے تمام امت اس کی حرمت پر متفق ہے۔
2 حضرت عدی ابن حاتم نے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم سے دریافت کیا کہ بسا اوقات میں شکار پر اپنا کتا چھوڑتا ہوں تو میرے کتے کے ساتھ اور کتا شریک ہو جاتا ہے اب یہ معلوم نہیں کہ کس نے شکار پکڑا تو کیا میں اس کو کھا سکتا ہوں۔ تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ تم نے اپنے کتے پر تسمیہ کہا ہے دوسرے پر نہیں کہا۔ یعنی اس کو کھانا حرام ہے اور حرمت کی علت ترک تسمیہ ہے معلوم ہوا کہ عمدا ترک تسمیہ موجب حرمت ذبیحہ ہے۔

امام مالک کا نقطہ نظر

و مالك يحتج بظاهر ما ذكرنا إذ لافضل فيه ولكنا نقول فى اعتبار ذالك من الحرج ما لا يخفى لان الانسان كثير النسيان والحرج مدفوع والسمع غير مجرى على ظاهره إذ لو اريد به لجرت المحاجة وظهر الانقياد وارتفع الخلاف في الصدر الاول

ترجمہ اور مالک استدلال کرتے ہیں ان دلائل سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہیں اس لئے کہ اس میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے لیکن ہم کہیں گے کہ اس کے اعتبار کرنے میں وہ حرج جو خفی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ انسان بڑا بھول بھلکڑ ہے اور حرج کو دور کیا گیا ہے اور دلیل نقلی اپنے ظاہر پر جاری نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اگر اس سے ظاہر مراد ہوتا تو سلف میں محاجہ جاری ہوتا اور (دوسری جانب سے) تسلیم ظاہر ہوتی اور پہلے ہی زمانے میں اختلاف دور ہو گیا ہوتا۔
Book of Slaughter. The madhhab is that it (the meat) is lawful (halal) contrary to the intentional omission of tasmiyah, and for that reason Abu Yusuf and the Mashayikh said that in intentional omission of tasmiyah there is no scope for ijtihad. And if a judge gives a verdict permitting its sale (the sale of that which was intentionally omitted tasmiyah), that verdict will not be enforceable because it contradicts consensus. Explanation: The Companions and the Successors are agreed that if one intentionally omits tasmiyah, it is unlawful. However, if one forgets, there is disagreement. Ibn 'Umar says it is unlawful, while 'Ali and Ibn 'Abbas say it is lawful. Since the prohibition of intentional omission is based on consensus, ijtihad is not possible here, meaning this issue is not one for ijtihad. So if a judge permits its sale, the verdict contradicts consensus and is unenforceable. This explanation shows that Imam al-Shafi'i's statement opposes consensus. Note: In some books of usul al-fiqh and in [Husami?] page 155 and its commentaries, Imam al-Shafi'i is excused extensively, saying his ignorance is not an excuse. His excuse is that he could not confirm the consensus. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: He has the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The Muslim slaughters in the name of Allah, whether he says the tasmiyah or not.' And also because if tasmiyah were a condition for lawfulness, it would not be waived due to forgetfulness, like purity in prayer. And if it were a condition, then the religious community would have substituted for it as in the case of the forgetful person. Explanation: This is Imam al-Shafi'i's proof. 1. The hadith that the Muslim slaughters in Allah's name whether he says tasmiyah or not; the hadith is absolute with no distinction between intentional and forgetful. 2. Rational proof: If you say tasmiyah is a condition, it would be like ablution. If one intentionally omits ablution, prayer is invalid; if forgetfully, also invalid. But you (Hanafis) say the animal is lawful in forgetfulness, so it is not a condition. And if it is not a condition, then intentional omission does not make it carrion. Also Imam al-Shafi'i says if we assume it is a condition, then just as in forgetfulness the religious community (millah) substitutes for tasmiyah, so in intention the millah also substitutes. The Hanafi proof: We have the Book (Quran): 'And do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' (6:121). This is a prohibition, and it indicates prohibition. And we have consensus as we have explained. And we have the Sunnah: the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i (may Allah be pleased with him), at the end of which the Prophet said: 'Indeed you released your dog and did not mention the name of Allah over the other dog.' He made the prohibition conditional on the omission of tasmiyah. Translation: Our proof is the Quran, the saying of Allah: 'And do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned.' This is a negation and it is for prohibition. And our proof is consensus, which we have already mentioned. And our proof is the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim, in which the Prophet said at the end: 'You said tasmiyah on your dog and did not say tasmiyah on someone else's dog.' The Prophet made the prohibition dependent on the omission of tasmiyah. Explanation: These are our three proofs. The Quran: Allah's command 'Do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' means do not eat those animals over which tasmiyah was not said. 'Do not eat' is a prohibitive form, which indicates prohibition. So it is haram to eat that which is intentionally left without tasmiyah. 1. Consensus of the ummah: before Imam al-Shafi'i, the entire ummah agreed on its prohibition. 2. 'Adi ibn Hatim asked the Prophet: Sometimes I release my dog for hunting, and another dog joins it; I don't know which caught the prey; can I eat it? The Prophet said: You said tasmiyah on your dog and not on the other; meaning it is haram to eat, and the cause of prohibition is the omission of tasmiyah. So intentional omission of tasmiyah causes prohibition. Imam Malik's viewpoint: And Malik argues with the apparent meaning of what we have mentioned, since there is no detail in it. But we say that there is obvious hardship in considering that, because man is very forgetful, and hardship has been removed. And the textual evidence is not taken literally, because if it were taken literally, argumentation would have occurred among the predecessors and submission would have appeared and dispute would have been avoided in the first generation.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling on an animal slaughtered by a Muslim who intentionally omits saying "Bismillah" (tasmiyah). The author first states the Hanafi position: the meat is halal in case of forgetfulness, but intentionally omitting tasmiyah makes it haram. Abu Yusuf and the Mashayikh emphasize that there is no room for ijtihad in this matter because the prohibition is established by consensus (ijma'). If a judge permits its sale, the verdict is void because it contradicts ijma'. The passage then mentions that the Companions and Successors agree on the prohibition of intentional omission, but disagree on forgetfulness. The author notes that Imam al-Shafi'i's view (that it is halal even intentionally) opposes ijma', but his excuse is that he was unaware of the consensus. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is then presented: a hadith that the Muslim slaughters in Allah's name whether he says tasmiyah or not, and a rational argument that if tasmiyah were a condition, it would not be dropped due to forgetfulness (like purity), but since Hanafis consider it halal in forgetfulness, it is not a condition, so intentional omission does not invalidate. The Hanafi response follows with three proofs: the Quranic verse (6:121) prohibiting eating meat over which Allah's name has not been mentioned, consensus, and the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim where the Prophet made the prohibition dependent on omission of tasmiyah. Finally, the passage mentions Imam Malik's view that the same proofs indicate prohibition, but the Hanafis argue that taking the literal meaning would cause hardship due to forgetfulness, so the text is not interpreted literally, as evidenced by disagreement among early scholars.

Key Terms
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The act of saying 'Bismillah' (In the name of Allah) at the time of slaughter.
متروک التسمیہ (matruk al-tasmiyah): An animal over which tasmiyah was omitted, whether intentionally or forgetfully.
عمداً (amdan): Intentionally, deliberately.
نسیان (nisyan): Forgetfulness, unintentional omission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on an animal slaughtered by a Muslim who intentionally omits saying Bismillah?
A) The meat is halal.
B) The meat is haram.
C) The meat is makruh.
D) The animal is considered dead on its own.

Key Takeaway
Intentional omission of tasmiyah renders the meat haram in the Hanafi school due to explicit Quranic prohibition and consensus, despite the validity of forgetful omission.

Hanafi Proof for Prohibition of Meat without Tasmiyah
Establishes Hanafi proof from Quran, hadith, and ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three proofs (Quran, hadith, ijma) that the Hanafi school uses to establish that deliberately omitting tasmiyah makes meat haram, and explain why the prohibition is binding.

Core Idea
Deliberately omitting tasmiyah makes meat haram — proven by Quran, hadith, and consensus.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi school's core proof that meat from an animal slaughtered without saying 'Bismillah' is haram when the omission is deliberate. The author cites three sources: the Quranic prohibition, the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim, and the consensus of early scholars. Understanding how each proof operates is essential for correctly applying the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three proofs
The author explicitly states that the Hanafi position is supported by three proofs: the Quran (Kitab), the Sunnah (hadith), and consensus (ijma). Recognize each as a distinct source of evidence.
2
Analyze the Quranic verse
The verse 'And do not eat from that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' (6:121) is a prohibition. In Hanafi usul, a direct prohibition (nahy) indicates impermissibility (tahrim) unless there is a contrary indicator. This forms the primary textual basis.
Consider how the imperative form 'la ta'kulu' is interpreted.
3
Examine the hadith
The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim involves hunting with dogs. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'You have seized upon your dog and did not mention the name over your other dog.' This implies that the permissibility of the hunted game is contingent upon saying tasmiyah. The absence of tasmiyah is made the cause (illah) for prohibition.
The hadith is a sound (hasan) hadith, though ahad, it is accepted in legal matters.
4
Consider the consensus
The passage claims that before Imam al-Shafi'i, the entire ummah agreed on the impermissibility of such meat. This consensus (ijma) adds further weight to the ruling, making it a definitive proof.
The consensus is cited as evidence that the ruling was established from the earliest generations.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
Based on these proofs, the mufta bihi (operative opinion) is that deliberately omitting tasmiyah renders the meat haram. This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon in fatwa.
There is an intra-Hanafi difference (Ibn Abi Layla allowed it), but the majority position is prohibition.

Source Text

كتاب الذبائح ولنا الكتاب وهو قوله تعالى ولا تاكلوا مما لم يذكر اسم الله عليه الآية نهى وهو للتحريم والاجماع وهو ما بينا والسنة وهو حديث عدي بن حاتم الطائي رضى الله عنه فانه عليه السلام قال فی آخره فانك انما أمسکت على كلبك ولم تسـم عــلــی کــلــب غيــرك عـلـل الـحـرمـة بترك التسمية

ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل کتاب ہے اور وہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان ہے اور نہ کھاؤ ان جانوروں میں سے جن پر اللہ کا نام ذکر نہیں کیا گیا، یہ نہی ہے اور یہ تحریم کے لئے ہے اور ہماری دلیل اجماع ہے اور وہ وہ ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور حدیث ہے اور وہ عدی ابن حاتم طائی رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث ہے جس میں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کے آخر میں فرمایا ہے کہ تو نے اپنے کتے پر تسمیہ کہا ہے اور اپنے کتے کے غیر پر تسمیہ نہیں کہا آپ نے حرمت کی علت ترک تسمیہ کو قرار دیا ہے۔

تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے جو تین ہیں۔ کتاب اللہ ارشاد باری ہے ولا تأكلوا مما لم يذكر اسم الله عليه يعنی جن ذبیحوں پر تسمیہ نہیں کہا گیا ان کو مت کھاؤ۔ نہی کا صیغہ ہے جو تحریم کیلئے ہے معلوم ہوا کہ متروک التسمية عامدا کو کھانا حرام ہے۔

اجماع امت یعنی امام شافعی سے پہلے تمام امت اس کی حرمت پر متفق ہے۔

حضرت عدی ابن حاتم نے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم سے دریافت کیا کہ بسا اوقات میں شکار پر اپنا کتا چھوڑتا ہوں تو میرے کتے کے ساتھ اور کتا شریک ہو جاتا ہے اب یہ معلوم نہیں کہ کس نے شکار پکڑا تو کیا میں اس کو کھا سکتا ہوں۔

تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ تم نے اپنے کتے پر تسمیہ کہا ہے دوسرے پر نہیں کہا۔ یعنی اس کو کھانا حرام ہے اور حرمت کی علت ترک تسمیہ ہے معلوم ہوا کہ عمدا ترک تسمیہ موجب حرمت ذبیحہ ہے۔
The Book of Slaughtered Animals. And we have the Book (Quran), which is His saying: 'And do not eat from that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned.' The verse is a prohibition, and it is for impermissibility. And there is consensus, as we have explained. And the Sunnah is the hadith of Adi bin Hatim al-Ta'i, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said at the end of it: 'For you have seized upon your dog and did not mention the name over your other dog.' He made the prohibition conditional upon leaving the tasmiyah. Translation: And our proof is the Book, which is the command of Allah: 'And do not eat from those animals over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned.' This is a prohibition, and it is for impermissibility. And our proof is consensus, which is what we have already mentioned. And the hadith is the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i, may Allah be pleased with him, in which the Prophet, peace be upon him, said at its end: 'You said tasmiyah over your dog and did not say tasmiyah over the other dog.' He made the cause of prohibition the leaving of tasmiyah. Commentary: These are our three proofs. The Book of Allah: 'And do not eat from that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' meaning do not eat those slaughtered animals over which tasmiyah was not said. This is a prohibition form which indicates impermissibility. It is understood that deliberately eating meat without tasmiyah is forbidden. Consensus of the ummah: Before Imam Shafi'i, the entire ummah was agreed on its impermissibility. Adi ibn Hatim asked the Prophet, peace be upon him, that sometimes I release my dog for hunting, and another dog joins, and I do not know which caught it, can I eat it? The Prophet said: You said tasmiyah over your dog, not over the other, meaning it is forbidden. And the cause of prohibition is the leaving of tasmiyah, so it is understood that deliberately leaving tasmiyah causes the prohibition of the slaughtered animal.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi proof for the ruling that meat from an animal slaughtered without saying 'Bismillah' is haram when done deliberately. The author begins by stating the three proofs: the Quran, consensus, and Sunnah. The Quranic verse (Surah al-An'am 6:121) is cited as a clear prohibition. The imperative form 'la ta'kulu' is a prohibition which, according to Hanafi usul, indicates impermissibility (tahrim) unless there is evidence to the contrary. The consensus referred to is the agreement of the companions and early scholars before the time of Imam al-Shafi'i that such meat is forbidden. The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim is quoted where the Prophet (peace be upon him) distinguishes between the dog on which tasmiyah was said and the one on which it was not, making the absence of tasmiyah the cause (illah) for prohibition. This is a strong proof that deliberately omitting tasmiyah renders the meat haram.

Key Terms
تسمية (tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' (In the name of Allah) at the time of slaughter or releasing a hunting animal.
ذبيحة (dhabihah): The slaughtered animal; the meat subject to the ruling.
تحريم (tahrim): The legal status of being forbidden (haram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary source for the Hanafi ruling that meat without tasmiyah is haram?
A) The Quran alone
B) The hadith alone
C) Consensus alone
D) The Quran, hadith, and consensus

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus to firmly establish that deliberately omitting tasmiyah renders meat haram.
